Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they call it in ancient times "contusion cure", and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II should all remove the forehead down towards the jaw, and the others II as II ribs above the cheekbones, and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are as II ribs above the cheekbones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of cloths for wiping the blood, then put the sharp spatula on two parts of this is the form: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the core which is between the two incisions at all its depth that is above the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second, and then extract further this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put it in the first groove the instrument called "cultellaire," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the rib inwards towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle fracture. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as eyes as long as the incision is continuous until that which opens the heart, and then otherwise make in the middle fissure until the other end; and then extract the blood evenly, and press their place for the taken blood; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and honey, and keep that pus pouches do not come; and on the third day untie the linen, and there administer great plant of warm water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	about the eyes  
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come catarrh acute customarily, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening of sight, and the nostrils burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in perform a pain acute, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh come forth only from many veins, and the maternal cure that is there, so is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great incision between the eyebrows, and another one through the wide space above the brow.   
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins with the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move toward the meal; and when the bone is discovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then dry between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, which cause flesh to appear. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of flower of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to prevent flesh from growing all over.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of stopping up of ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing thing such as water and oil and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or other manner of thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, if there distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and let him sneeze with the condiment, and stop his nostrils when the sneezes come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes by force with this treatment; and if it does not come by force, then they administer extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form. 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it is good to jump with the pincers, it is good; if not, administer extraction to the subtle needle of small doubleure; and if it does not jump with this, make a chain of iron and put the head of the chain or hole of the ear hard, and stop that which is around the chain with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter there with the chain; then the thing will be formed, for many times it comes to be as we have said; and if it does not come to be in this manner, take glut of that which is taken by the birds, and put on some instrument which is sharp for that purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the glut on the stone or anything else, and form it.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come from all these things that we have said, then hasten to flay the ear so that an abscess comes, and spasm; and the manner of the flaying is that you first make the patient healthy in the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and making a small flay at the root of the ear on the fat or where it depends; and let the flay be as a moon, until you come to the bone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.  
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is in and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer the spatula finely according to this form:  
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain.  
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with subtle pincers and a suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.  
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case therefore that water enters the ear it behooves the patient to use a first external condument, and open the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie lying upon that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she leaps forward by this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not, then take many stones according to the length of your thumb, thin and light, and heat them a little in fire; and place them on the patient's ear one by one, and they will rise up from his foot on the other side, and set a stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of stone upon stone until the water runs out completely, and so it will be entirely drained; and if you see, take a twig, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch fire until the most tender part of the twig burns; then make another piece of twigs until the water runs out, as we have said about the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the thing lighter to remove that is in the ear.  
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms, when you treat them as we have said in the division and treating distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then treat them with fine pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the snare of which this is the form. 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed gently to the whole pain; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to this, stuff the ear with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them who treat distillations; and distill your oils and your medicines in the ear with all these instruments, for this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or of iron, they are made small holes and above them so that it distills; and to press inside the distillation the instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap around its tip carefully cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and that which you want of your medicines in the canal, and the canal be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and feel the patient inside, and let the distillation be as much heated over the fire, so that it is distilled into the ear; and keep that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be so good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born that does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by the plugging of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes the poke of fire comes to the hole, and it is seen well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes to light through the ear, if one cannot see it, is of great healing in many positions, and in this one sees that you must place the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the hair apparent, then the work has all this spatula of what is here the form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it cut and sharp in front and behind entirely smooth, so that it does not scar the ear; if the suppuration is of flesh or the body of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut lightly, until all that flesh is completely removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take a thin and light razor and heat it a little at the fire, then put it into the ear's flesh. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the puncture, and moisten it in the Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this with no one day until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder over ground vitriol; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you pull out the tent and move another tent soaked in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are or treat distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of papers 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eye discharge that comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and are dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with forceps and tweezers, and the root of the spatula; then put on their place powdered vitriol.  
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without a decortication, he cauterizes with the subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision values to move; and many times they repair, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, they are burned those roots and do not return. 
de la gresle	of the ankle 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times in papers of the eyes come things that seem glassy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called “hail,” and it is an assembly of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the work is such: take ward if hail moves from one side and the other, and this is a light thing to know; then make the large opening, then the scraping of each part lightly, then take it with the tweezers, and cut.  
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without perceiving a little bit of the paper, do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the flesh restores it quickly and generates flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the stone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper, and hold the stone with pincers, and push it from one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not grieve anything; and when the stone is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place with that which generates flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is engendered in the webs of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to other people, and grieves them much at their eyes, and they come to have cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this they lie down on their faces and sleep, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two and feel the exirnach between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head in your health; and then take I the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains each part, then put it on him; and press with your two hands on one side and the other, so that the parts are assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula trenching a fissure of the wide, and not be more than large as the wound one makes to the vein; and make the leather in all its length until you come to the part; and in more dispositions comes the part from the fissure, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract therefore with a whole piece of linen cloth between your two hands outward, and turn your hand to the right and to the left as much as it is scattered; and keep that you do not add in the split, that you do not come to all the spatula until the eye, that you do not blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, so gently widen the split until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in hot water and cold, and put on top, and tighten with bands. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind seed and put it on to corrupt the moisture which is lodged. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place it is hot, so care with plasters soothing until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born hairs adjusted other than the natural ones, and are spoiled, they harm the eyes, and bring manners of maladies such as customary tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to IV manners: or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine ague according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done or by incision and sewing or by canes, according to what I shall say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to place the head of the patient on your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put a needle on all the thread above; and whether it is near the edge of the paper or the hairs grow near these hairs, and carry the thread upwards to the whole paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, to the whole spatula cutting, from the great tear to the small; then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then place above the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nonetheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who has need, then cut a large quantity of paper according to that which the paper is soft; then make across the entire spatula on the II lines that you have marked, and begin the cuts from the large tear up to small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the width of a root, then put the awl into one of the II angles of the heart, then peel all; then assemble the II lips at a stitch with a needle and all a thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make air to the superfluity of the hairs on the II eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care of it, then leave the stitch and the hairs until III days or IIII; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of them, but the stitch is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear; and if in another manner: and that you mark the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, to III awls opened according to the form which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut what surpasses the small forces evenly according to the form which is here. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle that has thread, and put it into the figure; and put the other thread near the big tear, and the second thread near the little one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then raise your hand equally, and raise all the skin on where you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, appease it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the splints is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the end inside according to what I have said, and then make II splints by art, and II subtle bonds as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the II heads of II parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above that which mounts on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the II splints of the II parties formed; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and tighten, until it hardens by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow to heal, if it is cut with strength, then care for it until it is healed; and when the wound is stitched together, and if the paper has been lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the II bones that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you prick a needle fine, and put in it the thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and knot them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase the other thread of silk briefly, and knot the chiefs of the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy one; and be behind the sun so that the work is declared clear, for it is a subtle and fine work; then put the needle all along the chase into the root of the hair raised, and make it pierce the paper quickly as long as you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all along the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you shall follow the chase down to all the length that you have ordered it, until the chase comes forth from the hole above and you see it by the sight of the eye; then you shall follow the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair roots in its place and the flesh grows on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany the long hair with those naturally covered, and be raised with that one or you leave it, as long as it is extended and then lift.   
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called “alecrati” or the rot comes in the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by suddenness of a wound, or a cut or cautery, and similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut open that suture, and separate its lips, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not proper that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Car if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but there is work of softening things, such as fennel; and the root of water or high and flax seed be cooked, and diachylon ointment melted in any oil, and it surrounds a tent, and cures with this.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not fuse according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing but directions for this illness, that it may not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is dislocation is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working in this is that you prick an awl, as it has double thread, and place it in the cartilage, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes into the II shoulder of the cartilage; then the cartilage is above the entire awl, and the scoop at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is proper, it is good; if not, then take the razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make II fissures where it costs inside the paper; and let the heads of the II fissures be at the II angles of the incision that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs are raised below, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the II parts separated, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said of softening medicines, and of tents, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain fissure under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is before; then spread between the two leaves of a tent, as I said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the sages masters equip everything with all their power how it makes the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in more dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the tightening of the paper 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to human hands in such a manner that the paper above is glued with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it behooves you to put the tip of a razor under the paper, and raise it upward; and the being as pinches, as long as you cut what is adhered to the spatula subtle, which should not be too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too thick nor bleaches the eye; and let your incision, from which you peel that assembly, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and thus heal that entire assembly, and do at no time in the saline eye water, and the soft water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wool moistened in oil; and after the third day use the collyrium and things until it is healed.  
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye  
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in two manners: it is nervous and similar to the hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and one wants to cure the pinches, it cannot; and both semblance begin towards the great tear, and cross little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head into your hand, then he opens the eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle at the pinches of small fold, and the upward; then take a needle, and put I hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and the strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a point and it into the angle, and pierce to all the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the upward, and scrape to all the hair the side of the angle which follows the prunele and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear to all the spatumile subtle and small forces, and let the flesh natural or tear, so that by incision come the body of tears customarily; and no time is the angle to the oncine only, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scrape on all the spatumile souef of what this is the form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a little bit of crushed silk, and from the collar made of lead, and let it until the next day; then cure it as much as necessary until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not tender, and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the probes cannot enter, many times this likeness of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see them covered, work the eye of the sick person, and take the spatula lighter pock sharp according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And put the head of the needle under carefully and if you see that it diminishes little or not, then distill from your mouth into the eye, a pill made with litharge and red lead and salt broiled, and plug the eye until the other day; then begin the other work according to this same work, as long as it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it, and first cure the abscess hot until it is healed, then recommence the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear hurts in the eye by great nuisance, then suspend it to the thread, and cut a part and not half total, that body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red water which is made of litharge.  
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the membrane which arises on the iris 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red and cover the eyelid and restrain on the papers and turn them to the fire, and it seems like a rose of balustrade; and the works if the patient put his head in his health, then the worker opens the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable instruments to those, and support it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go all cutting to the razor until the end, and guard that you do not blech the eye in the work; and let the incision be of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the angle and as small forces of which one removes the sebal, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silk ground or you distill red colier and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the eye fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be sure of a hot abscess; and if it remains nothing there, and the without skin covers you, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the abscess of things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make as long as flesh is adjusted in the eye by this semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you attend to the cure of each weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Certain veins are red that are covered over the eye, and they take away from the sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that you first look at whether the eye, in which it is, is or not, and there is no other illness besides the eyeball; therefore, coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your hand, then suspend those veins along all the body according to his wisdom, and be the threads subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form. 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then one coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye at the points of the spatulas, and make this work at hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut other than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remained of the evil. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all of these in that hour, make a plaster on the eye of things calming the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and the abscess is assured hot, then restart according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; and that is the form of forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and medicine of burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you should cut into the abscess where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the king has all the instrument of this which is the form; and it is called «aspre chief», and is made of fire iron to the head reont, and is pointed as a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it upon the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little while until you know that this corruption is set; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal drying.  
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the leus is soldered, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bow is soldered, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew and is not a bit suppurated, know that it is healed; if this is not so, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nef according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone the second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take the forest according to this form, and let the shoulder be of iron at three angles, and let the shaft be thinned down to the head as you see here.  
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone near the tear duct, and withdraw your hand from the eye a little, then turn to all directions until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes into this if he holds his hand on his cheek; and after restore the place of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the parts, so goes the matter to the cheek; thus it is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are wide open and they do not come together or diminish, then you must bind the patient; then the healthy one, then put the suction cups or a heater without hurting to suck, then put on the eye a poultice made of wool and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need; then strain it from above with a hard bandage, and re-start the suction cups to suck without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the poultice softens, then you must strain it much; then remove the poultice after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if no; then re-start the plaster and cloths and poultice and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the displacement of wool woven 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruption comes in the membrane stretched taut, then open it, and it comes forth like grains of resin, and it is easy to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is the double thread of the edge near the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then remove the needle and put on the other eye half in an egg white; and let it remain until the threads are joined with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, then pierce them with a subtle spatula which comes out from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and bring down the eyes, and enter immediately; then extract it until it is healthy. 
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye hollow 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called «alcunnati» is nothing other than a swelling which is assembled in the eye, seeming like a drop of water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on two parts, and move it as much as you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then be it fixed, and do not descend and be disordered the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bow is issuing; and when it is issued, distill in the hot eye water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that is boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the swords in the division, and what it is right to perceive; so in work according to the health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie their healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument that is called «almagda», or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument beside the cornea by the width of a thread in that whiteness of the eye to the part near the tear duct, then push the instrument that is called «almagda» virtuously, and thrust your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that «almagda» comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way «almagda» is at the point of the measure of the space that is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then squeeze it out drop by drop. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the liquid now descends, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.  
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water rises again by the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and it does not rise, gently strain the almagda by turning your hand back and forth; and then put back in water a little of seil gemme, and leave from this the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put with fire the eye covered or lined with oil of roses and an egg white, and tie it with the healthy eye.  
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put above as beginning with a plenty of egg.  
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you prick the instrument called “alberit,”  because this is its form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep in it, but make it subtle then put ointment in it as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with sleep beforehand, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be deprived of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to its disposition until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you perform this afterward because the liquid rises quickly.  
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and apply the remedy to that which soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed, then untie the view and put upon his face a cloth to cover for any day, and let it be so in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it goes out of the house back and forth, and converts into its cases; and know that none of the disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almond comfits, with which they suck up water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the shapes of an almond, for those who do not know them, they see them; and be from a grain properly. 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of these same subtilty, and the last in III angles acute.  
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the birth 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes limbs are born or become attached in various ways, so that some seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there is such one where the flesh is changed to dark color, and if flesh is of good color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these wounds which is swollen and not yet broken open, it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands opposite the sun; and open his nostrils, and place the ointment on those wounds, and let the pus come out; then cut that which you can support with a sharp subtle spatula on one side, as long as you know that the wound is completely removed.  
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains which one cannot cover, then open it all with the most subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it is without a summit, or abscess you close, or sew it as it behooves; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is seared and all the pus is removed, then pour in hot water or wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the mouth, know that it is clear; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is cartilage in the bone above, so that the instruments cannot come to cut: therefore you must put a thread of linen a little thick into it, and be anointed with hands of us, and have between each knot a space of a finger or less; and put the patient's shoulder of the thread into his nose at its tip, and pull in smelling until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is an easy thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other being careful as they are which are on the thread.  
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the men have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight to the place as before; do this III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the wound a caine of plank for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, to which one distills the oils and medicines onto the head: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of iron, resembling a lamp open, like a candle, and lead it thus; and if you see, so make a closed candle, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have the handle on the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the new 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
