Many times at the head of the nose is born a disease that is called "telul," and grows and becomes large very quickly, until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this, you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put on its place the cautery or medicine burning; and if you delay in cutting it until it is large, watch out if it is hard, of dark color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it at any time, it brings great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be all cut, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry things and restraining. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the vein is cut and closed 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuance comes in one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, because in no men.  
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that if this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two lips together with a suture, then care for it until it is healed; and if the lips are already dried on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, and restrain them, and powder over powder of dragon's blood, and powdered incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of ointment of strong or another healing ointment, and let it sit until it dries by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men, abscesses hard as beads appear inside the lips, smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut along each one, and take them with tweezers and cut them in every part; then apply to the place after incision of crushed vitriol, until the blood is stanched; and then the leave of aisil, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.   
de la char des gencives	of the gum 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a carbuncle is born on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; so you must hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let the blood flow out; then put powdered vitriol or other restraining and drying powders on the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens often, cut it a second time, and cauterize it; if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of deafness 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scales that are ugly and rough; and sometimes are the teeth black and yellow and greenish, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and are the teeth stinking; so it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or the scales as they appear, until nothing remains; and thus do of the blackness and of the greenish color, and of the jaundice and other spots, as long as they are cleaned; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, then begins again on the second day and the third, until you have everything pulled out; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to pull, according to what the work demonstrates to you, because the rasp with which one pulls out the teeth outside has other shapes than that with which one pulls in between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can with the extraction because one must not do it at all; for it is a substance very high until one has no excuse to remove it. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure the treatment, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain departs from the patient, and he believes that it is a tooth of Saint [someone], and causes milk to be drawn from the good tooth; and all the way does not depart the pain because of this, until the evil is gone, for we have already done this to our saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth hurting, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with all its spatula firmly in order to ward off the gums on all sides; then move it to your hands or tweezers with the first prick and prick, until it is well removed, then firmly affirm the tweezers; and be the head of the patient in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking, and if it does not come out further, take any of these instruments and put it inside each side gently, and move it as you did first.  
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, then it behooves you to fill it with tampons where the holes are; and if you restrain it subtly with pliers so that it does not break when you restrain it; and it behoves you very wisely to work around the gums to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore well guard that you do not break it, and remaining a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant healers who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the chariot and bring them nothing of what we have recounted; but often bring through the opening of these great maladies for the roots which remain there, or for the chariot which they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if a bleeding comes from it, which often happens, apply to the place vitriol powdered; and if this does not suffice, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, to which one puts teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles so that they do not double when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them have teeth to hold the hairs. 
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, then you must place upon it cotton moistened in butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are softened, then put the forceps called "algefri" into them, so that the head seems like a bird's beak; and be made inside like a file and this is the shape: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a palatine, because of this, here is its form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root leaps out by itself, that is good; if it doesn't, then with all your instruments, of which the shapes come after here: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two reins, of this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great pliers, whose form is here: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients do not teach an instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break the bone or the other bones, or it is possible, then there seek the instruments that it is necessary, which I have told you, and help with the gestures, of what this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but it can be held and removed; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all these instruments:  
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the body's natural form, and the shape is ugly, and even in maiden women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly formed after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or trim it: therefore, the saw; and if it is near with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and be of sharp iron on its summit: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope little by little in hands days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then the file of a type of file as this is the form: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing its tooth point by point in a few days lightly, so that it does not move until it chips; then the plain at the end to all none rasping, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bites the tongue, it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he moves it, and you have cured them with restraining medicines, and it does not work; then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and be the thread medium neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see it fit to straighten the teeth, take the thread and make a double loop between the two healthy teeth, then place the cheek between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you come wisely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the wires with pliers and assemble them, and place them between a healthy tooth and the one that is decayed; and then leave it so tight as long as it can remain; and if it comes loose, or the wires break, bind it again with another wire; let it stay and serve thus throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two decayed ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls, one puts it back in its place, piece by piece, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not skilled and suffering, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from deer bone, and one puts it in the place where the deficiency is, and one constrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.  
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this ligament which comes from under the tongue or nature; that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound joined; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue be dislocated from its place; and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from the soldering of a wound, so put the awl and cut wide that ligament; and guard that the cut is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the dew of rose water and of ease, or of cold water; then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind the patient every night, so that the place may not be soldered. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the running of blood comes, then put on the place pounded vitriol; and if the bleeding won't stop, then cauterize it with the lentiginout cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.  
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of rusty color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to whiteness and there is moisture, put on the ointment, and make it with a sharp spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the wound agrees with your work, put on powdered vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then raise the skin of the boil and of the seal, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils come inside the throat called "godath," and they call them properly the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and red color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid blood loss; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will split it, or it would break by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is subtle, have the instrument ready to cover, but first see if the abscess boils and is calmed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit facing the sun, and his arms be in good health, and open his mouth and place the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, for this is its form; and it should be of silver or fine steel like a knife. 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue of all these instruments, and you see the abscess, so take the one-chine and put it into the center, and pull hard upward as much as you can; and do not pull anything with the cloths, then cut with the instrument from here is the form, which looks like a forces; and nevertheless the chief are bent, and one place the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or d'andainne. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use pliers instead, for this is its shape: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side, and the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and salt, and if discharge of blood occurs, so gargle the patient with water, or apple peels boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stained; then cure it until it is healed; and some time other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them just like the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say the abscess of little sense; and I had well almost closed the entire throat so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained thus one day or two.  
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had to have been put two reins by the two openings of the veins. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore did so, and put one in the one incision, then I pulled out the thread, and in pulling a large portion of the bow; then I refashioned the other part in the other perforation of the two, and I worked its mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I put the incision in these abscesses, and in copied a part, and there came out nothing but a little blood; and so was opened the woman's throat, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting of this abscess for long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I grasped it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and know only that God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When grapes are gathered from the vine, and they are swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is small and round, it is called "grape." 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the poultice abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is round gathered and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it is necessary that you exhaust the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument about which we have made remembrance before; then put the probe into the eye, and pull it from below, and the cup to the one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use of those things that we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you should use an instrument to cauterize the feeling of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your breast, and then presses his tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with sharp, quick shoe so that it is not too thick nor too light; and in employing the end of this instrument, for this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the chief a hair or one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and puts the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles move from his mouth of the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the back; then hold your hand at all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it burning and the medications of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton is hard on the grape; and do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after IIII days or V And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, so commence it, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton buttered, and purify what is around the medicine; and be raised of cold water, and be cured with gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and aron and similar herbs, and assemble them all or any of them in a pot, and put it in there, and boil it; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have the instrument as follows according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or of iron, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the uvula through the vein, until the uvula is mortified; afterwards it begins again, until the uvula dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not make this except at the declination of the hot abscess.  
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put inside its head a firebrand of wood, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat; because the firebrand of wood does not make the vapor grieve the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or any thing, gets stuck in the throat; so it behooves you to pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is returned into the throat, it behooves you to make the patient vomit, so that the food may be cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will bring out the thing by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or the morcel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take the instrument of wood according to this form:  
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head held high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to him, nor push in the bone; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows if it is worse or easier; if he pushes down, or he draws it back equally to all the instrument, until it is far. 
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is medicine given to the sick without it being cured by medication; and when those do not help, then look into the throat of the sick person in the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you about. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the rupture, treat it with all small forceps or fine tweezers that are fit for it. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not worth it, then take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put where the end of the dog’s hair, make the iron hot, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And he endures water all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take full of cold water, and work the mouth, and put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he will fall. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I mentioned in the smoking of the grape; do this many times, for it will fall without hurting.  
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is this that you take a pot or it has charcoal vis, and let the pos be covered with a coverlet pierced in the middle, and in that one it is pierced the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes until the throat; and the throat will now fall, and if it does not fall, then begin again the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and drinks salty things and others, and drink no water; and then there is need that it should be gone by this government. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat wounds is, when it can be seen, like curved tongs to enter into the throat; and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and has roughness from lime, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the shape. 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to those that memory comes after from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in II ways one of which is in its own likeness, and of what it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the eyes which are in the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is other than that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if on abscesses one must not pierce until the bow is mature according to its completion; and if of such that it behooves to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses which are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and it is left as long as it is rotten enclosed, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.  
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; when it is near the foundation, pierce it also so that it be mature; and it does not behoove you to pierce an abscess before complete digestion, except for one which is near the foundation, lest it pour forth, and be lengthened within, and there come a fistula; and it may not heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the parts of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and the debate and the healing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more depending place of the abscess, and where it appears to emerge; and be the perforation of the long one of the body, and if the abscesses are at the hands or at the feet, or in joints and in nerves and in arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no flexion. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are dislocated, according to which member.  
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it's best that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.  
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce him in front of these, his body will be lengthened from the venom coming from him, and it is full of much filth; and by chance it hardens the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are perceived according to the width of the body, according to what the limb has need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut through the core, and cover; when it has become as soft as a sheet, and is dead, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils; and if there are such that are split in III angles, and if there are such that one cuts like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the limbs; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other sizes and seeming cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Whoever has no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; then stop the abscess until the next day, then do not drain anything directly; do this many times from great to small, until the pus is all gone; same if the patient is of feeble strength, or pregnant woman, or little child, or old man decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit is sometimes pulled out with the issue of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not concern yourself with it.  
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, so wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, administer dressings of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a dressing so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it inside, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shaving of linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then open it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then administer cold water and oil, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times.  
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer government and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it, as it is proper, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one must go before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter. 
des soros	of sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where boils on the head come small abscesses, and are of manners that are in webs, as well as the wicker of a birdcage, and there are many resemblances. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that have moisture as well as pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony in the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not do otherwise. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are such that you expect to every instrument which is called « entromissoire », of which its form comes after, what thing it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, dry it from above with a long cloth. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, then scrape without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns readily when one leaves it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and remove those that are left over.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed.  
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is held in the fatty tissue, so cut it according to this form, long; and put your tweezers on it, and the skin from all sides, and put all your care to drain the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you after.  
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with an abscess if it is festering, and of cutting and curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision upon the festering abscess and the moist one, is lighter because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to some of these abscesses or chief where it has no moisture, and of these I abscesses that I coped or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot be broken; and if one had made any, one would have done him as well a wound like a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, be it those that come at the chief of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be all days to the most dependent place, so as to better drain the pus; and treat them as is necessary. 
des scrophules	of scrofulas 
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess happens at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes it comes from another place or body part, and they are bad, and they are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrophule is properly inside its coating, like the pustule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrophules are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and some evil who do not want to obey sanctity.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that therefore you see of good disposition in the touching, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not at all bothered by the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; so it befits that you cut it above, and the peel from each side, and are the two lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the treat little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and be not too much the spatula or trenches, that the hands do not escape, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that stop blood, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to pus. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the skin is stitched, return to your work, until you complete it; then look with your index finger if there remain any small scabs, and cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrophule, it does not behoove you to cut that scrophule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no residue of superfluity for the size of the scrofula.  
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	So it is necessary that you pay attention to cover the root of it, and draw out pus, and treat it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulous abscesses that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; and pierce as that which is said before, in dependence, then administer bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then the cure of ointment, causing flesh, until it is healed.  
de squinance	of dislocation 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who made it, and this is the writing of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one does not help with these, because all the veins and pores of the patient are at these who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the throat channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV a small cut through, between the II circles or by the quantity of the cut of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no meat, and the vessels are long enough.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it behoves him to extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then split the gullet as far as it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe which comes forth from the place that is broken, and by the defect of the voice; and leave the wound open for a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound near the heart, and sew it completely single along the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is sound. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged to be dying, and that the fault is in the wing. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it has passed in III days or in IIII And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.  
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood which was issuing from it, and I saw well that it had not yet been cut vein nor lead but the throat, and the winds were passing through the wound.  
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I dressed it and stitched the wound, and cared for it until it was healed; and the young lady did not suffer any harm except that her voice was hoarse, and afterward she returned to her disposition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.  
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a wound, and it is very common in women; and it is according to II manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no cause.  
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat to us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work to do outside than in this one that is small, and the prove and seeks at all the introducer: if you find him as I fat, and cannot to any vein, then cut him, as we cut the fat, and the train to its whole top, if there is any; and encircle well soon, and cure it as it behooves, until it is perfectly healed.  
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, which I will say all the likenesses; and now it behooves me to say all the difference that is between us and outcome. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that pus is sometimes and fever-holding, as long as the boiling has passed, and the rotting is complete; therefore rest the fever and heat.  
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains I syfac, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a boil, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of this disease that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument that is called "entromissore," according to what its form will be or chapter which is after. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquisition of abscesses from us is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it is according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intromitter, and take care in those that will jump. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs short, whatever its color, make it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the needle moisture does not come, know that it is fat, so make it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and guard the coat where it lies that you draw it healthy with the new; and if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it remains there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little bit, and the wound does not grieve him, then apply to the wound some powders corrosive sharp, and restrain the wound, and put above soothing things an apoplexy hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the lump is great, then sew the two lips of the wound, and cure it with those who cause flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is beating against you, it is contrary, or otherwise haste and use the place of ground vitriol, and let it lie for II days or III, as long as the wound is festering, and rest the boiling of blood; then return to covering what remains from before.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the inserting instruments, and they are of III manners: great and medium and small; and there are III squares that are called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and there are of III manners: great, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistule; and they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron, or silver, and the most valuable are those that are yellow, and are more proven by black lead to surround the curves of fistule; and they are of III manners: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the tongs are many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are tongs which have II curves in III ways also; and there are tongs which have III curves, and are also in III ways; and there are tongs which have II curves, and tongs of one curve only, and are in III ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these has to do with cutting, and there are some that do not cut other than one side, with which one scrapes the skin; for this reason one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these intromitters are the alemeles put back in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are in III ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in their fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, and breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling a fistule scrapes, according to this form, for which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and place it once in its place that is suitable for cutting veins and arteries, and never return according to this great form.  
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they appear like women's breasts; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line .b. up to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and care for it until it is healed; and if it gets swollen down, and is softened like women have, then make it in two ribs above, by two similar cuts; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and let it sit until it softens the remaining tissue and fat, then care for it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the asses 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas which have ribs, and there are some that contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
