Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then use the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment afterwards to it as long as it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of a scrofula, then make it as we have said in incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound is rent inwards, then administer cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn together, many abscesses often result, and it also happens to an inflamed vein and abscess; and if one knows this is due to the artery, the abscess will be long in healing; and when you feel it on your fingers, you feel it strained; and when it is due to the vein, there are red marks appearing; and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is under the armpits, and elbows, and neck, and many other places, and is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It behooves therefore to choose the cure of iron, and that which is at the head it behooves also to choose, and in that which is an inflammation of artery by the top of the skin long; then work the waist as quickly as possible, and depart beautifully the artery from the webs, until it is discovered; then put below it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place which is between the II ties of an introducer as long as the pus that is there comes out, and let be delirious the abscess; then administer the cure that engenders bowe, until the tie lies; then cure those that ointment coming to these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, so it behooves you to hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there is I double thread, so that you drag it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or tie of one of II parts as II chiés of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads do not come out, so there reinsert another needle to all I thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and restrain the threads in IIII lengths; then cut the abscess as long as the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put on the damp cloth in wine and oil, then administer to them cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or by too much work, and similar things.  
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often as to the shoulders and to the hips, and in all their places where they have joints, and it is a grief abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one constrains it, then the patient feels pain, and is not at all in harmony with the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and that which is in joints ought not to be covered with iron: for fear that there might go contraction; and that which is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin at the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a rope, and scarify it, then drain it and suture the wound together, and care for it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and nowhere else; and it is a disease that is called «fungus» because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the roots are subtle, and the head is thick; and there are some small and some very large; and I saw the man who had II in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had fine roots, and they were slightly cut, and there flowed moisture from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found in one XVIII ounces, and in the other VI ounces, and the work in the incision is that you watch if the patient is moist, and the color of the limb is white and moist and of subtle root; if the cope with a wide spatula, and be in your presence the cautery at the fire.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the hip many times there come great spurts of blood, and if it does not stop, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a well-made thread of wool, and tie it on the limb as we have said, and leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the thread of wool until it heals the limb, and closes with it without effort; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut them all at once for the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the part that is of a bright color and of poor flesh and of milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess which has broken open, and I will come to its treatment after this. 
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound has healed 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery or a fissure of the skin and is on the belly and has some boils, like in other wounds, or from blood which cuts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse issue.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two ends it rises up, and then returns, and by chance it may be tight, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for great work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or wind. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must let the care.  
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then you command to the patient that he keep his arm, and be extended straight, then govern to enchase all around the belly; then command him to grasp firmly between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upwards to all the great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let it be joined by the ligament; then work the half of the abscess extended above the ligament, and put your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligament, then untie it, and put the intestine out from the outside of the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery makes itself contrary to you, or the vein, then go carefully around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II through threads, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross that you make pierce; then strain the abscess in IIII leus on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it may rot, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it of what is required, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is required, and weld the place. 
dou chancre	Of the ulcer 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of sores, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say the sore is prevented in the marshes, and great caution in the cure, and the ancients said that when a sore is in a place where one can erase it as a sore that is in the armpits, and in the groin, and similar places, and it should be removed entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black coal; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good position to do the work; then hit your incisions or sores, and the bone from all sides, and the flesh from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out entirely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped; then cure him with other cures until he is healed. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy  
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; this is explained only; and one must not touch iron in these II appearances: namely, tympanites and hyposarches, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this appearance of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and looseness of bowels and similar things; if you do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate: raise the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the spinal spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be cut from two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and however it should not be so deeply inserted that it can come to the intestines when it is placed inside, and do not let it bleed; then look if hydropsy is introduced towards the intestines: if so, you must cut into above the breast III fingers straight below the nipple; and if the hydropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then make your incision on the left side of the breast III fingers; and if it is for the spleen, then to the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and put it in, and lift your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as when scraping at a quantity of a fingernail or a bit; then pierce the syfac as far as the spatula comes to the eighth space, and this is the place of the water, then withdraw the tool, and put this instrument in so that it is the form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And is similar to a silver dog knife, and is of iron or arched lighter, and in the lower part it has I small hole; and on one side it costs III holes; and II on the other; and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision which scribes carve the pen:  
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than is due in this hour, perhaps the patient will die because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the liquid, and it is now held by the heart that stops the leak which is on the syfac, for that I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then begin the instrument again the other day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and treat of the liquid a little quantity; do this each day, and guard yourself from following until there remains not more than one drop of liquid. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you give him much water, so cure him of the burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and keep him from drinking; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.  
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No time is born a child who has no opening in the shaft, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, he must immediately discern with great care the entire spatula according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put in the small, delicate needle of lead, and tie it and hold it for III days or IIII days, and when he wants to make urine, then be removed the plug, and make urine, and then put it back; and perchance it is not necessary, because the urine which comes forth does not allow it closed.  
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, so are medicated with the balm of plantain, as we have said, and it will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in its place are bluish because none are born with the penis at the head of the shaft, for that reason they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the semen cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies flat on his back, and they are placed on the tip of the rod and the handle as well as the waist of a pen, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it befits; and take care of the bleeding which often comes, and if it happens, then the bandage of those who bandage blood, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albate comes to the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant; so it behooves you to seize them with the fine tweezers, and to cut them and clean them all, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of bad color and discharge, then you must bring it a cautery. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have caught it, and if the  bone is in its hollow, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it behoves you to remove the bone that is inside first; and when it is joined, then treat the one that is outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you make sure the head of the rod is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its rod and groin; so it is necessary to cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then lay on the plaster of honey and flour which is made of the bark of quince trees and dates, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is helpful for two dispositions: that is to say, bloodletting and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put or lead from the penis a cane of wood, and piss the patient among; and when the hair is irritated at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument's cheek, as long as the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any point of the head of the penis and the hair; then unstitch well between the two, and put in the subtle cloth of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not irritate further. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as other wounds; however, when we do this work of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for salvation. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have more than what we have acquired by experiment. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and surgeons who did circumcision in Dal, and with force, and all a new scalpel; so they fled because there are two cloths, and by chance if one strikes above and remains below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound should be covered, and the pain doubles, and in purification which is due to the blood isn't always assured the tip of the member; and in the purification of the knee by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they don't need purification and I have wanted it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification that is done with force to the whole line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, make it equally in I all soul tens; but that the filaments be well stretched around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be so that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the filament around the rod just so, and then allow him to rejoice in all ways that you can; then make him stay between your hands straight, and return the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the rod and blow or heart, and draw it upward until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below I poc to the other thread; and hold it as II does by the second ligation to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then lift the heart upwards gently and draw the head of the rod; then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the medicine; and put powder on top and above the powder the drapeil glued with a yolk of an egg cooked unsalted with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and let it remain until the next day, and cure him with another cure until he is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the fortification is this: the two shoulders are held and are sharp, and the shoulders are also as large as the hands equally.  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore, it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the flesh makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass III days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it be until the abscess has subsided, and the scab is lightly peeled; if you cut it as you can move it, and guard the part of the rod, it will not harm him anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place with things soothing plasters of powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one strikes too much of the core, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from the stone, or congealed blood, or bowels, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention for the stone which is in the neck or bottom of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on their knees; and they should put their feet on their back, and extend their belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient’s groin as much as he can; and therefore the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called “syringe,” of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine silver light like the feather of a bird; and the cane should be one palm long and a half, and fine at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of the urine is that you take the double thread and tie it at the head of the wick of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and alder of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis from above towards the bud; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and the patient feels it coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that because the leader or where it goes is twisted; then make the thread at all the wool head and head, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it and correct the urine; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient be aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood come in the bladder, or there is rot gathered, and you see it distilled with sharp and medicaments, so do it to all the instrument which is called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if there are III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leaves of the medicines so that they stop well the rod without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and push when it is necessary; and when you want to place your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the tube into the moisture, and draw with the syringe which is inside; so you will draw the moisture into the tube, and then reinsert the syringe inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: here it is. 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archut, and the head is higher; and below to the chest where the shoulder falls; then take a bladder of sheep and put in the moisture that you want to use to clisterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat the end of the moistor over the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the anus, then hold your hand on the bladder so that all the moisture comes out, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don’t have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it circular, and pierce it roundly; then put the strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dal, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.  
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all signs, and in what stone one must work with size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seemingly like water in its subtlety; and it opens up a hare, and makes the patient's penis heavy, and he thrusts many times, and then urinates; and with many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light for the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as much for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.  
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and pull them and move them downward so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and comes out of its place above; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely descending downwards; then feel it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall with the touch of all, so wet your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your right finger, align it to the neck of the bladder; then press up on your right, and put it out towards where you see the cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he press the bladder with his hand, and command him that he extend with his right hand the scrotum upward, and with his left hand lift the skin which is under the scrotum in the part where one makes the incision; then he puts the spatula cutting, because this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and be straight on the stone, and the two sides should be either foundation or support, and let the waist be so broad from outside and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large; by chance the press that is on the foundation, it may burst without work; and know that there are some stones which have angles and margins: such are hard to introduce; and there are some that are bowed, like a gland, and rounded, whose issue is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To those where there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, then it is necessary that you extract with tweezers which are like a file at the top, to constrain the stone so that it does not escape; or you put beneath the instrument subtle curved at the top; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the hole of the opening, and if the stones do not come out, strain them with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first put the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the trail down, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be stitched up, and a larger wound made.  
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through the place where his testicles cannot be joined; but nonetheless, you force to drain it, or to break it with pliers, as long as you draw it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, smear the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top a soft cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not untie the band until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you set it free, if there is oil and water, then treat it with dyacin ointment and basil ointment until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and by this urine is retained, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: all then you must do in the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn; then raise the wound of water and of ash and of silk, and help him in every way that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on top. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the duct of the penis, and stuck there, and the urine cannot flow; so the cure for this, as I said, is that you cut it many times, and an excuse for the cutting by this remedy. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this thus. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I iron rod according to this form and let it be three angles fixed into one stick: 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the forest into the rod gently, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand on the stone up and down, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side; soon will come the urine, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the rod. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is so broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents you, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod straight into the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and purify the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens at all, it is a serious ailment, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who unveils herself to the mire, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the woman's stone is more profound than the man's stone, so it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity appears to this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well-knowing, and at pains the true one is found, and if you don't find one, point so much as choose an experienced midwife; and present her with a wise woman in life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command from the inquiry of the stone; and look well that the woman is virgin: therefore it is necessary to insert her loin or foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she confines it under her loin, and recommends her to insert her loin or con with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the anus, where it appears protruding, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its sides above or below the stone, and let the tail be first small; then put the head into the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as much as the stone can issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the sinew is strained, put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the sinew is stiffened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is present, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone for men to help you in your work; and if the sinew is strained, and it is the artery that is cut, put the powder on the wound and strain it with bandages, and do not begin again this one, and leave the stone and do not touch it, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood is appeased, and the tissues become hard, then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm. 
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is under the yolk of the eggs, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have such a point.  
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is so weak that it comes to the joints, and that matter is spread. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses are reined, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess should be healed with part of the egg, and for this reason people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you suspect at all the intromissoire quarreit, because the form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what then comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on a thing a little high, and puts under him many cloths; then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the II ribs near the heart of the sides; then take the spatula, light, and cut the skin of the sides among them long up to the elbow, and let your fissure be entirely straight, dividing the skin of the sides until the white syfac, and the scar carefully according to your ability; then pierce the syfac full of water in the large opening, and extract all the water, and then put on your tweezers, and place the syfac upwards; and do not touch the heart of the sides, but only the syfac; cut all or by pieces equally the cost of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return the water; and if the bone is in your work, then set it back in its place when you have finished the work of the syfac; then assemble the II leaves of the heart of the sides with a suture, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the yolk corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the loss of blood; then cut the coil all the way to the suspender, and extract the yolk, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the hollow wound half in rose oil; and put outside another piece of wool soaked in wine and oil, and put it over the two points, and put on top doubled cloths, and tie it up above all the bandage according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two bandages, and use them of wool felt according to this likeness and be assembled by stitching in the crotch of the breeches, and one of the arms pricks onto the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two chief above the two shoulders, and let the whole assembly of the restraint in the buckle of the breech; and sometimes is medicine this rod of cautery in place of a sword iron, and it is that you prick the cautery blade subtle, and cut the skin of the genitals, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cope in all manners that you can, as long as you remove everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saving; and moves guarding from bleeding, and moves that the works of size; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or other things, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then administer a perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that the watery root is there, then make the patient sit on a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below all the spatula wide, and put the perforation long of the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave to drain the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you must pour into it a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water from the dropsy patients, of which the form is before mentioned; and enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is gathered after six months or until then, and when it is gathered like before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in more positions, for which it seems to me that one should let it be; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the genitals; and it is for many reasons. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by superfluity sour and acrid, which is spread to the buttocks, or from percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grievious fearful and painful, and of fuxe color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or from the swelling of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by the artery's vein, then it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess when you press it with your thumbs; and it does not behoove that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the inflation of vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the two, and can well make the cut on this semblance, and on the other chars; and that you cut the heart of the coins, then the egg is in high, and the train fur of the white syfac, and deliver the suspensoire of all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already solid with these new shells, then it behooves you to draw out the egg, and cut it; and if it is stuck in the syfac, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it behoove you to deliver all of that, and cut around it.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bone is or its rear, then it is necessary that you cut it all and remove the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, then use the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and in wine, then the cure with other cures until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a boil wrapped in a covering resembling the beard, with softening of the testicles, and the patient groans when he moves; and the treatment of this disease is as frightening as before, but nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then put the suspender of the breeches down to his knees, along with all the garments which are near the penis, and tie the masters together, and extend them; then cut with a sharp spatula wide through the middle the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then place a needle where the vein has come, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted moistors; then cure the wound as with others where one intends to make a bowe, so that no vessel is cut that nourishes one of the testicles; for by these there comes no harm, and if to all the vessels comes life, it is necessary to drain the testicles to all the vessels; so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot help themselves. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sciatic nerve 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is by the section that comes or in it, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either of the syphilis, or of the extension of it, and come these II ways of much cause: either percussion, or jump, or braise, or lifting of heavy burdens, and by similar things; and the signs when this is the extension of the syphilis, it is that they have poco and poco, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and is the abscesses even up to the parfont, for that the syphilis hastens the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the abscess, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are various appearances of abscesses under the skin, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the abscess. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it happens that the intestines are caught with the belt, and held in, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, even when it is pressed.  
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, for which it behoves to avoid it.
