Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is that you command the patient to bring the intestine to his hand inside the wound, if he can enter it; then be swathed on his neck, between your hands, and raise the hips; then put the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin long; then put into the sides of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the eyes can issue; then scrape the soft tissue which is below the skin of the groin, until the white flesh is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in what follows the groin, in what is between the white flesh which is below the skin of the testicle, and the second flesh, and depart from what is behind the testicle, and between the second flesh; and then move with your right hand into the heart of the groin, and hold the white flesh on top to your left hand, and raise the testicle onto all the soft tissue towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the testicle upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and ask with your hands if there is no intestine wrapped or white flesh hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the soft tissue, which is after the skin of the groin, after the waist; then cut the pieces that appear from the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the soft tissue, about which we said that it is below the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then wrap the pieces of threads, and tie them together in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except that an abscess may come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread II points of it, and after these II threads leave the soft tissue which is below the heart of the groin the largest of a point; and after all the others according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is below the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew, and the bow, as we have said before; then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put the thread that we have said there. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the white of the eye as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of the flowing of blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligament as long as it dries out through him; and if it lags in drying, be raised with hot water, and put above what we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to do the cure by iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the incision above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who operate, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it be healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a tear occurs in the intestines, as we have said, and it opens them; and let no bowels descend into the opening, and if any do descend, it is little, and heals all hours; and however if it remains too long in this point, then the wound or ulcer grows larger, as long as the bowel descends; and this happens because of the extension of the ulcer which is in the intestines, as we have said, because it is extended, then becomes softened and swollen the openings and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the skin of the tear inflated to the width according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the ulcer that is under the skin which you have cut, then take the thread and put it over the place appearing of the ulcer; and press it all along the belly, then sew the two appearing edges of the ulcer on top of the thread, and sew one and the other; then extract the end of the thread, and do not cut the ulcer nor extend the wound or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound as long as it is healing.  
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The wound is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the scrotum 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the veins that are inside are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary when one wants to cure it, to make the sick person lie on his back, and to cut the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, stitch first the superfluity of the softened skin to three sutures or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and throw away the thread. 
dou chastrement	through chastisement 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterizations are common in our law, and for that reason I would like not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one is that the healers know how to respond when asked about it and know the cure; and the other, because we often need cauterization of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and other animals.  
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that treatment is done in two ways: either by traction or by cutting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the joints are softened and pliable; then we take them in our hand, so long as they are set and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of the tail: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each side at the top, when you have well scarified them; and leave no prick or subtle prick which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing remains from the testicles, because the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as in men: the one if it is that between the two sexes opens as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes even short urine. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is on the pointed part also like a rod and they copulate. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of man and woman is that you cauterize all joined together, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine goes out through the skin of the genitals, there is no treatment. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a wart attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tetigine to your hand or on ones, and cut lightly; and do not go too deep in it, that hemorrhages do not come. Then cure with another cure until it is healed; and for another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and the empl, and by chance falls, and according to resemblance of a cow, and for this they called it the ancients “cowy disease”.  
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the origin, and cure it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of wandering 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and is natural by birth, or accident by illness that came to it; or it's by char joined, or by subtle or thick syfac, and is made through the midst, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever; and prevent conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the bailiff. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stroke is approaching near, if it pleases you to your two or to the right. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is dou syfac subtle, and it is close to the II leivres, so hasten, and do thus: put your II doe indices together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then make the II leivres form, as long as the subtle syfac is rounded, and it covers the estoupemens; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie at home each day, so that she cannot move.  
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the suture is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh, then suspend it to the sling and the cup; and apply blood-thinning medicines such as dragon's blood, incense, and a mixture with egg white; then administer a broad poultice of flaxseed, so that the wound may not close; and thus be lengthened, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other cures until it is healed.  
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes in the flesh, it must be treated according to this manner, unless it is an inflamed abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without accustomed correction, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thickened; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the piles, when they are driven into the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, unless by iron cure. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those that one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore you must put the woman in a cold house, then estent the altul as tongs and the cope in its roots, then powder with medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the air for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes out, so let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confiscate it with honey and aisil, and make a plaster on her back.  
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he withstands it, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not the case, if they are made to breathe with cupping glasses on the back and breasts without injuring them; then take linen, and moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and make them breathe there. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the harsh chief, so it should be covered as I said the thelul; and then the cure until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marsh 
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and stony abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It therefore behooves me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like the boils that are swollen; and if you want to know the work of fire, look at whether the abscess is large at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let him rest until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he leans, and supports his back and brings his feet towards the outer part of the leg; and let his hips be spread out, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good linen band; then lift him gently towards the right side, and there administer the instrument which is used to open the mouth of the channel, of which comes the form afterwards; and it is necessary that when you see administering this instrument, that you first insert the point in order to know the depth of the channel, so that what enters into the instrument does not go too deep, and that it does not pierce the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the channel with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument above, and that he holds the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and you make it with your hand soft, then it is fitting to cover the head, at the spatula lit; and when the bowe is emptied, then it is fitting that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green oil dry; and put the tent far from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and put by outside on the marsh and on the loin cloth clean moistened in water or malves be cooked; then cure after II days of ointment before this, as long as it is healed; and no time lift the marsh and the wound by clistere of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and aristolochia long be cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the mire, then it behooves you to guard against cauterizing with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth  
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of the natural childbirth, and the signs thereof are when you see the woman press downward, and desire to smell the air; then haste the child with force to be born; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it is the issue under its head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly her belly, so that the child issues soon; for when it descends on its head, then comes the secondine with it, and is cleansed the mother of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes at times upon his feet, and comes upon the body or the shoulders, and the hands, or where it comes upon his belly, or groin, and is converted by chance onto his neck, and by other evil figures; so it is necessary for the physician that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the powers of it are weak, then have her sit upon a saddle, or the women hold her; and apply its nature of oil or fennel seed, that is cooked, and then put the bail between its two buttocks with the small spatula which here is its form:  
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine and cut to its nail until the moisture inside is gone; and hold the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek muslin with sesame oil; then make her cough and sneeze with condiment, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will be born. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then it is necessary that you put them back gently a little and a little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on the seat, and lift her feet upwards; then throw the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall at the throwing down; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the neck which is put in front, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards; and then turn it back and forth, until it is even; then grasp its feet and stretch them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He can jump up to his hips, if he is commanded to take hold, and then make him sneeze with the condition; if he jumps further, may God will.  
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, there he lightly treats. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take muscle of the thigh, and oil of sesame, and melted wax, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make a collar of myrrh, and put it down there, and let her lie for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, because the child now jumps.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, then he puts the bail his hands here and there; then be it laid on its neck, and the feet hanging down, and lying on the bed; and folds its hands here and there, and then he takes the hands upon the belly, and removes the cushions underneath, until she is prepared downward; and if the child does not jump, then he takes his feet and moves them properly, then moves the belly upward, then puts his hands; and keeps the child here and there; and commands to the woman that she should squeeze as long as the child is passing. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who comes out with a hand wide  
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It behooves to try to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed, and unbend her legs; then administer the concoction that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try again to bring back the hand; and draw out the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to spit as long as the babe is born. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child upon his neck, and let his hands be spread, and his face turned towards the back of his mother 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient hold his hand, then turn it back and forth, and the elbow lightly; and when it is equal, place on the natural muscle of height and oil, as we have said, then command her to move back and forth; and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to strain; and the girl sneezes. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the back 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to being in this manner with the whole secondine, so strike the secondine on your finger, until the moisture is emptied; and if the infant bends up on its face and neck, so strike down from above so that it is not held back, and let the infant die; then put the infant inside, as long as you have put it as it is right, and command to the woman that she refrain any time: therefore, it will be lighter. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins  
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things and do not live if they have no name; I know these, that they multiply, and are separated by the syfac which devises them, which is joined to the bud; and sometimes they come out as naturally as ones all under, as we have said.  
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out with a shriek, so the cure as we have said, and let the bailiff be subtle, and make quickly and lightly what it does; and make thus as much as it is worth to salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of many children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	At times they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their sage glorious, and it behooves the bailiff to know all this, because by chance things happen; so it is done according to what befits.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands; so it behooves that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; so it behooves that the woman be supported on her back, and her shoulders inclined down, and her legs raised; and the minister the woman from II parts, or she be tied to the bed so that she not be troubled by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils with muscillaige of altee and fenugrec and seed of flax, then anoint the hands of her hands with these oils and these muscillaiges; then put them into the womb lightly, then desire I the place where she puts the pins that be suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appeared that it descends on its head; so stick the pins in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, so stick or prickle and at the middle of the ribs; and it behooves that he holds the pin with his right hand, and puts the curvature between his fingers of the left hand, and puts it all her hand lightly, and sticks the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then fix the other bone opposite it, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then place them equally in moving from one side to the other, so that they may move freely, and let the bones be toothed to hold them together, as is the form here. 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part of it, so anoint the bailiff with some oil from his fingers, and put them in that part, and draw the other part; and if none remain, put this one on higher or above its place, and do this until it goes out entirely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, it is necessary that you envelop it above the drape, until it is all; then cut in the joint of the plant or at the knife, and so it is necessary that you do in the other hand, and as II feet.  
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is swollen at the end, or it has a sharp point assembled, then you must insert the pointed spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the sharpness; or you will run it with the instrument which is called “almidach,” because its shape comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the child has a large head naturally; and then draw out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and is strained to the force, so it is split, as long as the moisture which is at the bottom of the end comes out; and if it cannot come out, you cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs.  
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, the traction is light, and the delivery at the mouth of the womb is easy. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is strained in the belly or in the breast, then you should pull it out with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and make the belly or breast go as long as the moisture that is there passes; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then push the fist into the center of the marrow; and draw it until the mouth of the marrow; then put in the thread or the II, and draw out the thread; and if the mouth of the marrow is tightened by a hot abscess that has come there, then it does not need to be worked on; but moist and fatty things should be given; and apply plasters, and wet and softening ones.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, administer what we have said in a living child; and if you cannot, then treat the limb by sections, and leave nothing of the second kind. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the patient has boils that come in the marsh; and if bleeding occurs, it should be put in vinegar restraining, and administer other treatments.  
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the swelling, and it inflamed so much that it opened and began to great purulence. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long time, and could not solder the wound. 
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a strong plaster on it, and after some days one bone protruded, and after some other days another.  
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much amazed because this one whose belly has no bones. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cauterized the wound, and in treated the bones so that the woman was in a better condition; and the woman lived long enough like this, and always had a little bump of flesh there; and I have not recorded this chapter for any other reason than that when masters find something strange, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the bone to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the clamp, which is described in the books; and to its two heads the two limbs. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft I must be wide, and the edges of the trees I must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a bit more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the harness to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar in appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pliers; and have the two heads II adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and II wide; and when you see open the jaws of the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and her legs open, then put the II adjustments together in the jaws, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand to the whole instrument, as you have done to pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the jaws, until the girl does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the one looking at it has seen them appear, then is the work more hasty, and higher to men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disdain the instrument, so long as it is well prepared for it its necessity is not excusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it behooves you to command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well is it. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not so, take a pot and make it perforated or covered, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put one end of the chain or perforated pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and keep it there until the vapors come inside the marsh; then make him sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second bone leaps violently. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no strength, command the midwife to soak her left hand in sesame oil or in alum lotion, and then put it into the vagina, and push hard; and when she finds it, she grasps it and pulls it gently back and forth, so that the child does not fall during extraction; but it should be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled; then it will come out and disengage. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is too tight, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not use the milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie it to the hip of the woman, then give an enema of tetra-pharmacon oil; if it will bear and return, and come to cure; but anyway, when it bears it comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and pale the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are needed for these: none of the ancients have experienced the efficacy of fumigation with watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument for which one fumigates the woman to restrain the flowers and the womb is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire; and let the fumigations over the coals, and the tinder until it is burned, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the bottom felt, but it is stopped by a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife that she pierce that syfac with her right, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the lacement that she does not touch it; then put on linen moistened in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will set right again, then put in a piece of splint and leave the limb for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at times this stunning comes from the hardening of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that hardening; if it is cured, as we have said of the cauterization of lead.  
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation 
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come from near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and even moisture awakes white or subtle bowe, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and they are known by those who have them or excretion or windiness when the patient makes excretion, and perhaps in jumping some. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if to fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and reach up to the juncture of the hip, and up to the root of the groin. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing to the base, and not passing; and it is that you put your index or foundation, and put a subtle needle of iron or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is a twisting, put in a tent of fine wool, or horse hair, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out through any emission or ventilation or air, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so haste to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the channel of urine, if it leaks urine, and cannot be healed by medicines. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the tendon coming to its place; if there is no tortuosity and invention of pain around, then it is that there is a bowe in it, and it does not merit medicine or treatment by ointment; and in these fistulas piercing there is no cure except for labor, and vanity of foolish wonders who intervene in them. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither young nor old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined to his belly; then put a tent of iron, or of plank if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, you should put your index finger there, and as soon as you feel it touch it; and be uncovered or where you feel between your finger the tendon or the flesh, then know that it is pierced; if you don't work it, one cannot cure it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says nonetheless that one can well heal some, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one makes, if it is done, one cautiously heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and he puts all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred hairs are burned, which seem like a feather of an eye; and then the cure with damp compresses in butter, as long as those char marks are gone, then the cure with ointment healing flesh and sewing. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so, he is well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, otherwise it cannot be cured; and if it protrudes between, and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your two parts and the protrusion a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula after the covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the protrusion, and then the cautery afterward, until it reaches the top of the protrusion; and will be delivered the protrusion, and fall; then remove those fleshy tumors that seem like a bird’s feather, and nothing remains. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound pains, and comes between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of these attached parts, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the cure of tender wounds in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the parts are burned inside the wound; then cure the wound of sudden boils by encasing hard flesh, and medicines are dry. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is reset, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the foundation, and is distant from the body, put your finger on it or its base, and inquire about it. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between II is the cloth or the syringe or chariots, where it is near to piercing, if there are no others but way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and care as first; and do not go too far in parfont, that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and let the egestions come by lay will; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound once she is cut from below her foundation, or by tent or by another instrument appointed; then clean the char faultree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so it is a lighter thing for the sick person. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you place the tent within the fistula, and it is or sits against the base near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts the thread wrong in it, and puts the tent at all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.  
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that one pierced, as you put your back or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and hold them to each other, and let it be for a day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads close those pieces that are between two, and come together; then cure the wound as long as it is healed and cured. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in every way that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make the lace for covering if they are so embroiled, and then care for it, as we have said, until it is healed.  
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spathula spine from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and trenchant; and on the other side no, because this one does not cut that which one should not cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids 
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those which are outside have little moisture, and still, a little bit of clear water or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment of those who have them within the foundation, it is that you command the patient to lie down for air in chambers, as long as the foundation issues, and appear the threads; if you hurry, and can hold it with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold it because of its moisture, so take it to the cloth, or to cotton, or from a piece of felt; and take it out with your hands, then cut it, and powder above some hot powders that be in lieu of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery; then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundation cannot issue, then clistize the patient with a harsh and sharp enema to wash what is at the foundation, so that it may issue openly; when the patient gets up, and if the threads are out of the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you take them with your finger or with pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that it fears the incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the stitch in this manner: take I thread, and put it into a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the II ends of the thread below the needle, and so be of the large; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave I to correct the superfluity of blood; then put on top of the foundation I draping moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and place it on top, and command the patient that he rests; and then leave him until they dry out, and when they are dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of fluids in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not useful.  
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it become moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, begin scraping again stronger than before, until it heals well and is scraped; then treat it until it is healthy. 
dou fremit	from trembling  
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants is a small appearance falsely before the body, and goes much in harm; and sometimes finds it cold, and feels him also like dead from tremor, and comes into all the body, and more to the hands than other parts.  
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a caine of a goose feather, or a very strong vulture feather, and put that caine on the skin, until the purple circles touch the skin all around; then turn your hand all over the caine until you cut all around the skin, and put it in perfect place, and scrape the skin from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do as follows of a hook of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above. 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not feel anything, to keep on holding tight, and pressing it 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is a clyster made of silver or lead, or melted iron or mesh; and never are these instruments, small and large, made according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are treated in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small. 
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema tube small and great is this above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a detachment where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head of the shoulder is pierced inside; and has on one side II openings, and on the other I; and the belly is where one puts medicines from the bladder of an animal or parchment, and is pierced all around with small openings, and there are I spaces between each opening, then put into these openings I strong thread of thick thread twisted in X or in a circle, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie the end with a strong thread in front of a thread, then use an enema; and this is the shape of the circle:  
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And be the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief from the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently; then squeeze the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all seen, then remove the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it so as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night entirely, then there is greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him with a laxative for a stomach ailment, and the medicine quickly departs, so let it return until he is healed.  
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are either at the foundation or an abscess, so let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is strained. 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the care of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.  
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from that which they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and cutting of sword and knife, or spear or club or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
