Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is from a stone of similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is large, and you doubt strongly of an abscess hot: so I do immediately bleed from the cephalic same even if there comes little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the contrary side of the wounded part; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and fatty meats.  
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to bleed, let him reduce his meat, and drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in a vin stiptice; and if there is no abscess hot, he puts on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, that I will say a little later; and if the air has moved it, put on some ointment, until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then bring them together by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered of bone, and hangs, and holds on only by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, also as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a skin rot, and it does not reach the bone, so cut away all the rot, and throw it out, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie up the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which joins as soon as the fire has touched it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and restrain it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then cover it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with caulks alone, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has cauterized the wound, even if it is still raw, do not put on this powder; but apply some digestion ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it softens; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you afterward about fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes at the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.  
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other way but to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerve and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of them is with the brain, which is the most high member; but let the medicine be warm, like lukewarm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumel lavée also in lukewarm water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.  
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind with bandages, then treat until it is healed.  
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is capped and full of flesh, then pierce or lower down; and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes out, then stop it, and tie it up, and cauterize as is needed; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduit is guarded, so that the meat goes, then sew the heart on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then restrain it carefully, and leave it for several days, then cure with ointments as long as it is healing; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then fill it; and if there are pieces of bone, then pull them out all that you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound decays, and be free and aligned its exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, so treat it as I have said in my chapter.  
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife 
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then see if from the wound there is wind whistling as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh to all its blood, then do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not clot, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there comes no spasm, nor bad tremor of the heart nor strangeness of breath; and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.  
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure therefore with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, and work, then see that there is a fistula; if so, treat it as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, then the cure of those in front; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deep into the bone, and pieces are broken off, then cleanse the wound, and bring out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, leave the wound to rot, so that it will release; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound, sometimes the intestine or nerves of the intestines come out, because of which there is an introduction of others; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, for this reason one puts the intestines back in more carefully; for that the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, they go back in more carefully, and for this reason, the medium wound is worse, because of this one puts the intestine back in its place like the others. And know that the rupture of the belly is in four ways: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other special sutures are common to other wounds; and all the same, they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one for each and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines has come out, and it is necessary to close it, this is done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in boiling water only, or you boil in hot water with squill and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine as long as the swelling is removed; and no time do this restraining thing, and it’s moved that alone to deflate. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and malves be cooked, for by this is aligned the entrance a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that tail, which none should cut except great necessity is there; and this is the instrument for splitting it; slice inside in the curvature and outside no, and see here the form:  
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails protrude, you put them back in their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, because it is worth moving. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put what appears to you, then have between your hands the minister pitiful that holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of sutures, and is that you prick an awl or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound I distance, and there put an awl where it has the good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the siphons, which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that side, and assemble the II heads of the siphons the IV together; then the strain of a double thread around the awl of the II parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound again, and then leave I distance, and there put another awl; then tie the end of the thread as you have done with the first awl, and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles, until all the wound is constrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: for that reason they should be medium; and it does not behoove to put the needles too far out from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and there put tents or drapes on the heads of the needles for them to hold, and leave them as long as the wound is sutured; and this manner of suturing with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there suffices one needle or II for the second suture if it is common, and is that you assemble the II heads of the skin and the II heads of the siphon together on an awl where it has the good medium thread; and when you have pierced these heads all IV together, turn the awl to the part where you have begun, in the manner one sews the fabrics; and put a space between each suture the thickness of a small finger; this suture served the man, and I sewed a wound on a horse's belly, which was wounded by a knife, and was the wound more than a palm wide, and it was out of the intestines well II palms wide, and was the wound in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestines after they had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed up to XV days, and I treated him, and he was well. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the people had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one did not find any, nor any medicines; and I put more above the wound cotton old II times a day, and I washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the core straight through, lay the point of the needle down where you have put it in, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you stitch as the furrier does the furs, and that you leave the point of the needle on one side, and take it back on the other, until the stitching is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which the Galicians call properly, is like any font, which assembles the two parts naturally together, and applies one chief to the other, in such a way: pierce an needle or chief of mirach prochiene, and make perceive that place alone, and leave the two chiés dou syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part to that inside, at the two chiés dou syfac; then make pierce the one and the other from the outside part to that inside, in two other chiés dou mirach that are on the other side; and this is the middle manner of suturing and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens thus says this word, and no one testifies it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must thrust one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corded things; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the others of the belly.  
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of the other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh to all its blood, so long as the arrow has moved it, then put back the intestines, and the outside; then put on powder containing char, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bows; and bandage the thread, and be soldered the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to close, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in many arrangements while the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make commonality with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten linen light in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the flanks, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in bulbs, and many times happens, then give clysters of black wine, and even if the rot comes up to the intestine; and pierce it within, and know that when this is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called «jeun» cannot heal when it is ravaged, and this is because of the planting of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the wire jumps from the wound, put it back as though the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to black, you must tie the part that is black so that bleeding does not come from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the tied part, and place the two heads hanging down from the side of the wound outward to align the extraction when the wire falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, because I saw a man wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and through this there was discharge and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop treating until it was healed, and the edges joined.  
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient had badly in his belly; and there was no evil, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and said any experimentors that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such manner: take threads with great heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has covered the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it strains its mouth above; and then cut the head, and it stays so that it cannot untie, then put the other thread after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is burned inside, and there comes no nuisance to the patient, and one can tie the intestine of a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this gut thread that is well cleaned, and then tie it to the head of this linen thread twisted finely, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and move it in the rupture; and this way of suturing of the bowels is not surpassed except according to the way of marriage and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing else or saneness, except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is closed and inward curved.  
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth knotted fault-ridden hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes thin, and other times enough; and I have already spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the IX causes: this is to know, by the smallness of the blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to be born; or there is too much bowe; or the matter is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and slow healing, and inflamed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is therefore necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by hand.  
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so that it comes to the property of the principal member, and to the similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you want to know it, so take a tent of iron or iron, if the fistula is straight, so the curve; and if the fistula is crooked, so the surround with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends well around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents, so clench it by one of the openings, because moisture comes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then look wisely at your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and it is sewn in depth, and ask the sick person about the pain he feels when pressing your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places that I have told you, so operate according to what I have told you, and remove the bad tissue and corrupted matter that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in a straight place, so it is necessary that you cut it as deeply as you can, then put moistened tents in medicine of vinegar, and put them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is remaining at the bottom; and then put ointments for healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not hurt you or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then treat the surrounding flesh so that it may be healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns like before, know that you are not yet well done: if uncover and continue until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.  
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot reach it; if there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can drain it with tweezers, then extract it with an instrument suitable for this; and if there are many bones, then drain them all, leaving none behind; and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put upon the wound something that will prevent rotting, and let it remain until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily loosen; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, let this corruption reign only until the blackness is completely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it comes to the marrow of the bone; it should be treated and covered all the way up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is fused; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work.  
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about XXX years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, until the materials came to the leg, and it became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the physicians, out of their folly, operated so much that the abscess opened, and they corrupted much matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many pores that all flowed pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated him for about II years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called upon him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what oozed through the pores into a great deal of the body; and the young man's body became red, and had a yellowish color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore inserted myself into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I saw what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I had removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not heal it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and was going to suture the place; but I couldn't even when I inserted myself around a palm of the bone, and the tract was throughout its entire length, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healed and quickly sutured, and did not have to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the blood evacuation often happened, but it was cured entirely, and in the place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was in good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary at all, neither to going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it is necessary to be treated in this manner: take linen, and strain it at the head of the bone that opens, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and put another linen band thicker than the first linen, and tie it above the flesh which is below the bone, and stretch the head so that you pull the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh in the place where you see to be, so that the skin does not cover the flesh; and put a coal or a piece of wood under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to be so long as one can see and feel the corruption, and be again another time.  
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely; then put the fire under it, and then apply the fire from one part to another of the corruption, and let the cloth be as long as the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and apply the fire to the bone where it contains it from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else than to cover; and if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand or in the thumb of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that the instruments to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their fineness, and their grandeur and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so consider the instrument which you need according to what is right. 
dou feu	of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be injured due to internal or external causes; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, then comes the corrosion of the limb member to member, and takes hold of the whole body; therefore hasten to cover, and if it is due to the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, you cover at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, you cover at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there are no remedies but the quantity of its virtue; and so do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes in the first joint, you cover after the other joint; and if it comes or foot, you cover the whole foot; and if it goes up to the leg, you cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way than to let the patient die; and the manner of covering or treating the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister one of the bandages down, and another minister the other bandage up, and you unravel the skin which is between the two bandages to a spatula wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then cover or treat, and put on each side a cloth of linen so that the dressing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place thoroughly, or put some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion first came in his heel, until it possessed his whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long afterward the corrosion returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are corrective after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of correcting the matter; and also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired of everything, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this story only so that one may do otherwise, if it is necessary. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus bursts out, and it remains like a vessel; and the skin which is above is as subtle as fine linen, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called “Sain”, and is not called “fistula”; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone or even through it, then it is called “fistula”; and the skin is that you cut all around that skin, and even when it is subtle as fine linen; and does not heal for its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you think that the skin is hardened and the corruption is not yet fully formed, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat it this way: look if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, then administer a clyster of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take asafoetida, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and administer it as a clyster to the breast, and hold the anus closed; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by straining; do this many times until the breast is softened, and the odor is removed; and sometimes administer a clyster of ash water when this medicine is not present, and that is to take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it and administer it as a clyster until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then administer a clyster of water and honey in which there is a pinch of ground litharge; or you can administer a clyster of honey and sweet wine, for the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes it dry; and when you have done this, and you are convinced that the breast is well cleansed, then administer a clyster of what causes flesh to grow in it, and that is to take diaphinit plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can administer a clyster of certain medicines and ointments, about which I have spoken or treated in the treatise on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment or basil ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then sew and leave only the place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening which stinks is above, then place the cup or lower than that.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is in place, do not let anything interfere with it; and if you cannot cover the breast as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the bow goes to its lowest position, because when the bow is in place, do not let anything interfere with it and if you cannot cover the breast as you wish, arrange it so that the bow moves slightly downwards, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and put a linen sheet covering the entire wound; then cut the forces exactly where the opening of the breast is a little wider than the first, then put oil under the other sheet according to the amount of the opening, and place it on the wound to align the bow, and do not remove the large sheet except after many days once; and the one that is on the opening of the breast, often remove to remove the bow, and know what runs from the bow, if it is venom or a little pus, or digested, or indigested; and take notice if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in this manner and you see the nature that jumps on the wound of the breast, then know that the breasts will be healed soon, and approach health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other sheet, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed ingestible after many days, know that the breast does not heal well. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venoms come after a long time, if it does not trouble you of health, for the health approaches.  
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and some who do the opposite; and if a swollen breast is felt after many days, know that the breasts are not healing well; and if the breasts are slow to heal and are painful, then apply medicines drying moist ones in substance and dry ones in virtue, such as diafine ointment, because there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diafine ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of old wine equal in substance; then boil it and use it; and the same thing is done better by honey boiled and mixed, when diafine ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue it to the breast, and put it over the breast, and no time administer a long scalpel and roots of celestial lilies, which are also like flour of rice and wormwood; and use either simples or composites: grind them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has gone too far, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard limbs, or on the members; so the cure of a fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then comes the abscess red, and runs and hollows out so much until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps even all of it; and the corrosions come up to the bone, so that there comes a pungent pain, and the limb becomes hot and swollen. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity which is left of the wound, then cauterize the wound afterward. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to pierce it, and bleed, then it is necessary that you put the root under the nail so that the flesh does not pierce it, and push it up, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with dressings until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it, and treat it well, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that it is about to corrode, then cut it in I as we said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and bruised, and he feels great pain, then you must heal him first; then cut the angle of the spatula sharply by cutting across above, and warn that the cut does not come down to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on it which soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder from the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance there is some where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us of the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any kind of a nut, do not move, and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance moves; the size of him who is fleshy, such is light, in this manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: so keep it from being cut. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In someone who is born or must have the afterbirth removed, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh around until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, then cure it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The soldering that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by soldering of wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things. 
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut that joint, so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not join together; or you put between two pieces of thin planks, until the limbs are joined, as it befits. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joint comes together with its palm, so bind it as is fitting.  
des vils	of the evils 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels full of melancholic excesses, that come in multiple limbs of the body; and there are more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It therefore becomes necessary for you to administer to him once purging of colocynth, then a potion from the basilica. 
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two manners: one is to cut it, and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and treat it all the way. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The hip is treated in this way: first, raise the leg of hot water very strong until the swollen flesh is softened, then hold the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; then cut a vein in that place, in I or II or III, with a wide incision; then lift and draw forth the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the sick person can endure; and then bind it up, and command him to stay on foods avoiding black coles; and restart the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harm the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner: put the leg of the sick person, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it at the fire, and then cut the place above the vein from the top of the knee to the heel; then work the skin with your knife and scrape the vein on each side, until it feels open when you touch it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white rope; then put the tip underneath, as long as it is lifted from the skin, and then place it on the knife lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it feels open, then raise it with the knife, as you have done before, and place it on another knife, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the top of the foot, then treat and lift until the second cut; then straddle from cut to cut, until it is all pulled out, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle into the whole strong thread double, and tie it and pull it, and put it underneath the tip, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, because if it breaks, you will not be able to pull or lift it, and it will cause annoyance to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put a piece of wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twisted, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.  
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it only cuts the vein; and is of a large curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the shape. 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is created in legs, in hot parts where no herbs nor trees are born, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it is born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of rot that comes under the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes the color, and begins the vein to go forth as a root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
