When the head of the shoulder opens, it behooves you to wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half up to II III., and tie it, and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that it is point at the defuer, it wraps around the plank, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it in its root, until it is entirely out; for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings an abscess and rot there, and bad disease; so that thing behooves that it be treated little by little up to chief, and nothing remains of it in the body; and there is sometimes this vein when it is treated from V palms long, or X, and one hon came to me, whose it was from X palms long, and when you cut it, it put I ray out or percus, and pierces it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and be emptied of the matter which is inside, and administer at the place medicines against rot any day, then cure it like abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes in this vein the blood rains, and even when it opens at the joint of the foot or the foot, and there comes much of pus, and from which it jumps blood; cure therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body moving up and down, and one feels it well at the edge of limb by limb, as long as it leaves the skin where it goes, and leaps further; and it is engendered of rot of some humors, such as come worms and snakes and filth and roundworms of the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.  
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him cured and treated, it is only possible to heal it when it goes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong ligature tightly bound, then cut above and treat the wound further, and if it comes back in the flesh, and you don't find it, then cauterize it with fire until it heals; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, bind below it the eyebrow, then cut above, and treat the wound further; and it behooves to use the patient of cleansing of the body with medicines solutives for the humors carried, and avoid eating meats that cause putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, like hot silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then shortly after spread throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she felt it returning back around her body, as I saw.  
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this sickness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had wanted that well have moved pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and veins uncovered, and for that appeared that constraint of windiness; and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then lie above and below carefully, and then cut upwards as much as the windiness is constrained to its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with those who expel windiness, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they enter. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some that have large points, and small ones, and haired ones, and joined; and those that have II angles, and those that have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one which falls in any member so it falls according to II manners: or in principal member like brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, that I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: then it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not gone through, then treat it, and cure the wound.  
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow enters and pierces the bone, and jumps the syfac which is above the brain, it is when scotomia and sode and esvertin and red in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without flux from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice; and jumps from the wound moist white seeming to poultices, and jumps also like burnt flesh; and if this sign appears to you, hold off from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves also like the finger, and in short black blood comes, and coldness and sweaty cold, and fainting: know then without doubt that death is approaching. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the common is that without pains of foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the sick turns color, and sighs high and seeks the cold air.  
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the flank, it is near the small ribs; and casts great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulder. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes or stomach, by adventure there leaps out from the wound some thing of undigested meat. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls or into the belly, and in no place of bone through the gut, there is no hope for healing, nor in the extraction of the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaps and comes out, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder joint and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and the seeming members, are safe according to more disposals. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason that you do the same thing. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that went into the root of the ear: I held it and pulled it out on the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was cured without feeling anything. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And there was treated one wound in the fat of the eye below the paper and the arrow was put back, and one could only reach the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was great as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the player was unharmed, and did not have any bad accidents. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I treated an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I extracted the barbs, and carefully removed it until I pulled it out, and the Christian became healed.  
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow in a man who had it in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then after passing thirty days, it did not change its position; I cut on the arrow, and burned it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow shot into his back, and the wound is healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural positions, nor feels any inconvenience in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, who had an arrow shot into his face, and the wound was soldered together; and he remained so suffering great pain; and many others like it. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow to the man of princes the king, that it was in his side near his rib, and was a little sloping to the right part; and the arrow was whole reponed I was called to the cure after this that it fell three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with an entirely subtle touch, and I did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on my hands for days and sutured the wound straight, and kept the patient there a long time, until he felt the arrowhead in his nose one day; and he told me that. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive and sharp for many days, until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which was hardening in place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it remained well for IIII months, and then enlarged so much the wound that I put in the pliers, and moved it on one side and the other, and could not take it out; therefore, I did not cease to refine and invent ways of instruments, until I took it one day with the pliers well made, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: therefore I restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take everything; but the wise masters compare to very little thing, and on those that are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not found in the limbs where they are fixed except according to II manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that is by the place where it enters, it's an arrow entering into their flesh, and there is no other time. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it be so until the flesh is healed around it, and ease its exit; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot move out, let it remain like that for some days, and moisten it each day; and then when it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, pierce around it with a fine tool until the flesh around it is opened up, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not draw it out, but leave it there until it is equal after a few days, because if the arrow comes to the syfac, it is death.  
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone only, and does not come up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the engine of the milking.  
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very tight like this and cannot move further, then administer poultices around it, as I have told you; then care for the place until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is placed back in its place in the body, if one cannot see it, then search for it with all diligence; and if you feel it, then treat it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot, due to the width of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then widen until the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck between the two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out; be careful not to break the arrow, so that you draw it out more easily.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, lay it until the place is softened, then treat it, because extraction hurts. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes you contrary, so administer that which we have said of the cure in its chapter; and guard yourself from the incision of the nerve and of the vein, and put engine how you may move the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow fell into him, for that is the greatest help that there be, and if you cannot, so place him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one cannot see anything of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that it can be seen or felt obviously: cut therefore above, as long as the pincers can take hold, and then extract it; if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it still further, and then resume the extraction until it is drawn out; and if it is of the arrow there, put it to the whole shaft; and if the shaft is broken, and you see to administer a thrust, then administer the instrument in the way that the tip of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then thrust further, and if the arrow is driven, then push the instrument to the point entering inside, so as to ease the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is surrounded, it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or to the bladder or to the ribs and it is close, and you can cover above, then strike it; and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if need be; and cure until it is healed.  
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the shape:  
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.  
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the hair is also like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as it is in form. 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers to insert and to know if it is here: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins that one is cured with, for which there are XVI heads, namely: two batans that are after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the two veins that are on the collar; and the two veins that are in the upper lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are below the tongue.  
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which are commonly drained are V in each arm: one is the cephalic and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is on the bone, and is the one which is drained, which opens clearly on the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the sap vein is the one that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two of them; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the first is below the curve of the pocket of the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse," which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.  
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and with migraines; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their places depending on the head: so you will put your hand, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, so sign it; then take the lancet, and push it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein upwards, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two fingers wide, and make blood flow as much as you see; then strain and tie it until it is cured; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for old migraine, and sudden, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of tears acute eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient restrains his neck, until the two veins appear clearly; and feel the vein below your right, and then sign on them; then raise the heart above the vein in your right index finger, and put the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and the cut, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a correct amount of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then the ligature forms, and let it stay until it is healed; and we have spoken about them and their cutting and their extraction, as the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein on the forehead is as good as that of the cephalic vein for old facial diseases, and for migraine, and for redness; and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur," whose form is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and firm with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood issue according to the quantity that you see; then tie the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and no time the wound of a wide flame.  
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper for the flame to be too large; and the healthy side across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flame when it is thin. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the II veins that are in II tear ducts so helps as the eyes, and to the chin, and to the cheek, and to the inner corner of the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein, and whether the vein is through the traverse, a prick of the long of the flame a prick wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then make correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie above with cloth, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for ague, and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and red rash that comes in the face, even when it is old.  And the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his neck, then pulls his nose with his left hand, and takes a fine long flame, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not let it go too far, and make it flow blood according to your need, then tie it at night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps in the treatment of the spleen, and in the beginning of melancholy, and many diseases, and in epilepsy, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and estiomnes; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient holds their neck as one and both sides, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient lie on the seat, then open a vein of the long one quite widely, then draw the blood moderately, or as much is needed; then redo another part in the other vein, then untie the lien, and restrain both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until the morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins of the lips above helps in the ulcer in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and in toothaches and pain
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein so is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and know them by those that they are black, and by those that around them small black veins: cut therefore both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and also do with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The veins under the tongue help after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is to the constricting of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a vein black: bleed therefore one and the other, and do not let too much be taken out, for beneath are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins to be cut from which one commonly heals are healed in two ways: either by pricking them at all the flame very thin, or with a subtle olive as sharp as trenchant blades, and it is called "lancet"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and depth of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame martin is very renowned, and is wide as you see. 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and full of thick blood that appears, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame.  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.  
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the belly; and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and that he beware of the artery that is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the earth, and running of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; and it must not be pricking the flame, but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you constrain it, and change another; or you want any vein of it, or you open in its place the vein in the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cup to the flame anesil, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then thus it is fitting that you draw out the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame vessel; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery: avoid therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the veins are red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and put your finger on the length, then remove your finger if the vein is stretched, which often happens; bind his arm, and leave thus, and do not move him, the patient; and be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the artery is not stopped and it bleeds, and you do not have medicine there, stop the artery as soon as possible; and staunch the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a cork of pistachio, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well until the next day; if it doesn't get stained, that's good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the stanching is not griped in more dispositions for the small place of the wound, and the force of the ligature of the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps that it treats blood from the top of the head and from the body below, for this reason because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic as we have said; and it is necessary to the healthy one that he put himself toward the nerve which is below, and if it is not too much in length, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the saints be burned, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you probe it with an instrument. and examine the nerve to your power.  
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make it long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head helps so much that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is good to bleed by pricking at the olive branch or the myrtle branch because it is the safest of all veins, for it has no tendons nor nerves nor arteries.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and it does not matter if one fails the first time, and one starts again; and by chance, it swells for some men, when one fails the first time, but it does not matter.  
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, if it is administered only to keep health, and to avoid diseases to come; and be the bloodletting done in one of the three veins which are or cut: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent on foot, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to maladies has no set time, but when it is needed by day or by night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not proper to blood children until XIV years, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Let not those over sixty years old bleed. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some wants to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract the useless superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor should one bleed him who is too full of meat, or who is drunk, as long as he remains so, nor those who are dropsy; and worse it is to bleed after colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, vigil, and fasting, and all that which weakens the virtue, either by thing of the arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if he has them large, by meat, by drinks, and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids you, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist or near the third finger, as we have said; and guard him that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things; and be he tied and joyful, and let the blood-letting be higher than the one who bleeds, and rub his arm twice or thrice, then restrain the linen above halfway, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood well; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the blood-letting with a little bit of old oil, then put your finger of your left hand on that vein below the wrist one inch where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not burst and fail in bleeding. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are like cords in the healthy person, and there are some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, therefore it behoves the healers to be aware of these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below that place or above where it was inflamed, if the place is not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the  leg is swollen, and the patient complains, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: by chance there may come boils; nor enter into a bath, then restart the bloodletting if he pleases; and if the opening is small, or the vein is thin subtly and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, fire in that same opening all the flame straight; and work a hole gently, so that the leg is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not start bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil over it, because it closes the body's blood, and it is thicker in this place than the oil; and thus administer the oil on each vein that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing works for triacles and boils, when you put it on the place; so subtile is the blood and separates when it is too large.  
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is only cleaned once or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place on top a sponge soaked in water and some hot oil, and restrain for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days, no blackness or greening, so it does not harm him; and if you see, put on top anything of aloes or myrrh applied in juice of calament, monstastre, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance to the basilica’s vein occur: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance bad.  
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put on anything of what we have said, because by chance it may come short of the artery; but let me plaster it dry to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.  
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is full and robust, and needs the extraction of blood, one should make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; and to him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed little and often, and one must bleed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is more useful than the bleeding through the long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to one whose body is deficient in blood, it behooves to give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if it is hot, treat him with blood III times or IV. And if he is of cold complexion, he will take moist bread before the blood, in quince syrup, or in honeyed aromatic syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pricks at the vein, after the outflow of much blood, then it behooves him to soak a sponge with broth of flesh and subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the opening of the vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to empty his arm after the first vein, and he has strong flesh, so he heals seven hours after the first vein, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third.  
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body that has already been drained, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the incision as much as it will go into the palm of your hand; then when you have rewarded all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his pulse when he heals, that death may not come in place of the palm, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see the arm disjoined, and make blood flow for a second time, and the incision is closed, that you press hard; nor if it is curved, that you extend the arm as much as possible, because it would be bad; but leave it until he heals a second time; or to the point of the flame, as long as the blood that is frozen at the incision of the vein flows out, and put on top the point of wool put back in sharp, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it alone and do not restrain it, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to draw blood a second time, then in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein emitting from the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composed. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the bone is red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then the vein is opened through, neither short nor long; and let the opening be wide, and let it be opened close to the joint of the hand, and if one cannot make it flow, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood running in the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back into hot water, because it is put in more in winter than in summer; and the vein of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.  
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting of the vein of the right hand is good for all maladies of the liver, and here's how: restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if you see it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it completely through, it does no harm; and do not let them go too deep, because the nerves are under all the flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot flow out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you will have treated of the blood as much as is necessary, so put on the vein oil and wool to sew firmly, and thus do for each vein. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of him in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have said to you towards the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sap of the sophene is good for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the leg, and retention of flowers, and disease of the hips, and thighs, and old legs, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its healing are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it aches, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; heal therefore the one which is more prominent, either at the ankle, or to the foot, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, so guard the nerves that are below, and heal by traversing as when chopping; and let the flames be unbridled. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be released, then put his foot in water, and let it drain well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first incision is necessary for the sinews, begin the second one above a little bit, because the tissues are salty; and do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and so make a similar cut on the other leg equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle of pain, and its hurt is worth to the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood.  
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its blood are that the patient enters into a bath and is strained over the ankle four fingers by twisting it, because otherwise he does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you heal it in all the ways that you can, and by traversing; and it is better that you let it heal than to cut it off, because the vessel is dry and she is very well-repaired with man's hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy no vein of the one who opens or back sore foot, and toward the small thigh, and guard the nerves; and make as much correction of blood that you see, and then untie the band, and put cotton on and hold it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of leeching 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.  
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done to wound is according to II manners: or it is to all fire, or without fire; and cupping which is made by wounding and by extraction of blood is made in XIIII leus dou cors, for that one is all in the chief; and the other is emmi the neck; and II others in II costeis dou col; and the cup on under the chin; and the cup on the II shoulders; and the cup on the hips; and the cups between the II arms; and the cups on the II legs; and the cups on the II ankles; and cupping does not treat of blood, but only of small veins that are spread in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anything, as is done with blood from a vein; and it is not appropriate that it should be administered, neither to all fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bloodletting, or for customs, we bring them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are some who, when they have need of bleeding, have a heavy head; and so that some feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness to the eyes; and such who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and bleed; and there are those who dream, and see by blood and numbness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed after three hours of the day, we command to be ventilated. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the head helps in the greatness of pain of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is not fitting that those who are of cold complexion in use, or who have catarrh, because this does a lot of annoyance to them; and for that reason it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those who have or head colds illnesses. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down out of fear of obliousness. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of pain, and for cutting the channel of the throat, and all, and for filling; and it should not be pushed too hard, because if it is held too firmly, it causes obstruction in the stomach or heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The punctures of the II ribs of the neck are good for pains of the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the operator that he expresses his hand when putting, that he does not cut the artery, and does not come hemorrhage.  
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Mouth ventilations under the chin are good for mouth illness, and gum rot, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the veins of the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for the illness that comes from heat and fullness. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The phlebotomies of the armpits are as valuable as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from those large veins; and instruct the patient not to apply too much force, because the skin is bare of flesh, and it lies over nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids at their root, and for diseases of the anus, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large, and be made of bronze, so that it needs to milk well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and thereby it makes great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs should be applied openly because they draw blood from the whole body and are good for old pains in the hips, thighs, bladder, and soften the tumors; and they are placed on the two shins and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring numbness in many dispositions.   
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and successively, and put it gently, and move evenly, and do not cease to do this, until you see its place red and inflamed, and appear the redness of blood; then firm, and put back the suction cups, and take ward in the disposition of the body, because there are those who have tanned flesh, and clear pores: so it is fitting to strike once only, and it is fitting to make large wounds, and a hole deep; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to pierce it twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick the third time; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we only suffocate once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish much blood, often let us restart; and if the veins are thin, make them thicker with a fire stick, and the end is that the hairs be pierced suddenly, and it behoves him who has thick skin and hard, and who has wide pores, to oil the cups of oil appetizer and dissolvent: If it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or cucurbite seed oil; and if it is in winter, of cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or a similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of amber, or of balm, or of anise, and similar.
