Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to whom one is healing has tender skin and large pores, there it does not behoove to put any oil, but it behoves to wash after the ventosation of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or something similar.  
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise from it, or from water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities raise themselves with old wine, or of their own water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things; and it is not proper to suck blood before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or II; and do not sleep after the suction, and it behoves them to rise, when they should be suctioned and when they are suctioned. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is healing is bilious, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; then it is necessary that he eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce at the bowl, and similar things; and young chickens, and mutton, and moist meats.  
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey and scented wine which is between old and new, and cumin and nutmeg and small onions and pigeons; and the day he will be bled, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men once triacle or musk before the bleeding, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let it be subtle, but it does not behoove those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without injuring are those that are placed on the liver and spleen and gout and on the belly and chest and hips and groin, because these members do not suffer from being injured on themselves, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, such as when we put them on the breasts when the child is born; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and chest to reduce swelling; and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or displaces the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind; and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with lukewarm water, such as in diseases of the pleura; and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water that has boiled herbs suitable for it. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered to fire is here: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two pieces of wide and half palm in width, and has or on the sides around the middle a small hole, as if to put a needle, and be of iron, so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb; and has in the middle a bar across of iron or steel, to put a burning candle, and they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the cups of children are other than those of old people, and of the thin ones than the fat ones.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this suction cup on the limb: grasp the candle of wax or linen, and place it in the suction cup across from the rod which is inside the suction cup, so that the light be at the bottom of the suction cup that it not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and the tes are to be on the perforation that we have said, so that when one wants, si goes the vapor, and one removes the suction cup; and grasp the linen as before, and restart it often, if you have need.  
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered in disease of pleursin, on all acuteness, it has no handle nor spike, and is administered only when it is full of fluid, and is placed upon the limb solely; and this is its form. 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not administered except in members where one cannot place leeches because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar; and in the exposed flesh, such as two or three, and other similar things; and the qualities of using it is that when you find leeches that are in sweet clear water without dirt, take them; and put them in a nut of sweet water until they become full, and have nothing in their bellies; and then purify them by vein and leech cup, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put the leeches on top; and when they will be full, and swell, if it is the place where one can place a leech cup, put it there, because it is very beneficial. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, raise the place of it carefully, and then with water, very well, and then bind it; and if the parts are healed too late after the body of the wounds, so moisten the linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the wound is closed; and if the wounds are multiplied, put on crushed vitriol, or salt, and similar things, until it is closed; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry out on the place, so now will stop; and if you need more of this, take other wounds.  
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds will not be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle there until the wound lets out, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will open; and when you see that they are weeping, sprinkle on a bit of aloes and silk ground up, or ash, so they will now close. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear child, that the fool mire look at this chapter, they never saw any of the old books, nor read any letter; and for this cause is estranged science in our land, because I never found any good; and know nothing, except by the science of the old books, where I studied so much that I treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have made you known in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and showed clearly the forms of the instruments which are furnished, as I have done in these II chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.  
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his tension is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say, cold meals, and meat of hare and kid, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; then may the patient return to his first government that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great swelling, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and kidneys, and entrails, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such a cracking of the bone, it takes more time to heal and the fracture is faster
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken of the old and the decrepit do not well rejoin or solder according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, like the bones of small children; but make no care, reset on the broken bone I strong holds which support and join the limb together, as much as it forces it as it was before; and for that cause one must nourish him with big meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to a roll, and others that sharpen like the point of a feather for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with a fracture there is a wound, and a fracture to all a little fissure. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its engine and its tool proper in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which the bones are twisted, and open well by outside, and son at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor pain at touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not appropriate for you to move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in a bow, and the two parts are disjointed, it is necessary now to put them in equal alignment, so that abscesses may come; and if abscesses come, let him leave none a day, until the abscesses are calmed; then put it in equal measure as you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this one is lighter than the restoration of him who has pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary after. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it's from two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or to your hand if it's a small limb, or to two cords, or to one cord and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you will reset by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work does not come to the patient injury nor pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.  
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if you straighten it beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come from their work abscess hot and contraction of the limb, as we have wished many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient that he not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither turning nor in any other manner; and guard well that the limb be so secure that he feel no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	Car when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it behooves to put it in such a disposition that he feels no pain; and keep that it be put straight, that tortuosity may not come when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard linen cloth, because the wide linens embrace all of the large limb, and restrain it on all sides evenly, so that there is no gap; then tie around light bandages, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and strain your hand a little on all the linen, then go above the fracture and strain less, than the fracture then pushes away a little from the fracture; and soften the linen a little at a time, until you grasp a large part of the healthy place, then take the other linen, and turn back around to the top of the fractured limb; then return to the part below the fracture, and strain it moderately, neither too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put between the linens bandages of linen or cloths, so that they are all equal, then tie everything on top with a bandage, and then put your well-made supports on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put upon it a soothing poultice for the abscess that heals and lets it subside for some days; then press upon its stitches with bands of half a cane's width skillfully cut from a stick used to make staffs, or from palm rain, and let them be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is necessary for the limb of small size or large; then restrain on the splints as you have done at the first hour, then tie above a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; more tight it is above, less; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the thread are thick, as I want from the works of fools who make their ties with cords of twisted linen, and this is a great error, because the tie cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not become that there be between each splint less than two fingers’ width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore by the joints of the shoulders after the straining in their healthy places, then put beneath them pads of linen, or wool cloth, so that he does not become bruised.  
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the bones are broken, I will say its cure here afterward.  
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it does not come well to put poultices for after 5 days or 7, or more according to your certainty of abscess arising; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour which remains at the walls of the mill, and confis it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, neither too bright nor too thick, and use it, and it is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many dispositions, and also to women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take abrasives, and ladani, and enule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mugat, ana X III; myrrh and aloes, ana V III; alechil VIIII III; and make it into powder, and mix it with yolk of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, he uses this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones well, and is good for many men.   
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of emplasters that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana X parts; myrrh and aloes, ana IX parts; acacia VI parts; Armenian bole X parts, and grind them well, and confit with water or egg white, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaistering to joints and bones out of their places, and soothing the pain arising, and the size used in bone, and fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in water and oil cooked, and put upon the place.  
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes the pain. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making a poultice that mends broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a poultice. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remaining pus from an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of quince, one part each; and grind, and confection with wine, and if the member is scalded, confection with moist coriander water, or water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of splinting more forcefully than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.  
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrates says in his book that on the broken limb one should put a restorative made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put on the broken limb, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and the heads of men's hair, or goose feathers, and wormwood, and seland equally, and grind them, and make a poultice with it and apply it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if the bones have not moved from their place; if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and sponge of wet sea, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie above a nut, as long as you are sure of a hot blister; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be removed the pain, then begin the fine binding, and a little plaster, and do not constrain it so tightly as before; and make it subtile until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and painful and swollen, I have removed it completely, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, if it starts again, as you did the first time. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there comes to the member nothing of what we have said, then do not unbind it until after III days or IIII or V or VII; and at no time let it go XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals, and approaches the adjustment of the bone; therefore restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see it drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; arose then water hot, all times that you unbind it, and let it be every third day, and moisten a little the wound; by this work therefore shortens the nourishment to the member, and mends quickly what do the foolish fools, who leave the member twisted: this is bad, and so is working fearsome, and I do not see anything else than to leave it and to work it straightly. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse manners of fracture 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures there are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made from the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone all the bone up to the place which is below the bone, as it is made high or pole-axe; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts bone from above without piercing, and is called this manner of fracture "absolute"; and the wound of these II fractures great or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow embedded, or fissure or of collarbone of stone, or of cheek on stone, or other similar things.  
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is great or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound which is put back in the bone as subtle as a horsehair, and the fissure is small, and for that reason this fracture is called «capillary»; and if the wound which is made either by striking with stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and brings the piece of bone inward, and are the legs like those who do the blacksmith when they forge on the cauldrons; so between the stones within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or whose chief is moist bones, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are scattered in them like stars; and I will speak of it in its place.  
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquiry at tents, and by the rotten cartilage which is upon.  
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair capillary is known by those who when one has uncovered the bone, and rubbed against it, so the black fracture appears. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes is to be red and inflamed, and other similar ones in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no danger of accidents, and you hope for salvation, so begin the cure. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can.  
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, so hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day,  so that the tissue under the bone may be corrupted, and come the accident that we have said. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you divide the broken part thus: and that you prick the head of the patient with a needle, and uncover on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more deeply than you can, and if a bleeding comes out when uncovering the bone, or an abscess appears, help it with what is necessary, and fill the place with moist cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess appears to be calmed, and be sure of the stopping of blood; then begin to remove the bone around, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you cut at a narrow incision before, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts another piece larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and be pointed, and be of iron; and in work lightly, so that you do not injure the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dry, then it is necessary that you pierce it into it, so that you administer incisions with awls, lest they go through the bone beyond, and it must have above the point a margin or circle that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and it is necessary for you to have several of these, so that each one comes in its place on the thickness of the bone, so that you may have awls for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of awls: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to feel around a broken bone is that you put the tarer on the bone, and turn to your two sides as much as you know that the bone is felt; then put the tarer in another place a little after, and so do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and make them more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, it is fitting that you reset the apparatus which is removed from the bone to all other instruments seeming like a chisel, but it is fitting that it be more hardened and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or no scales, then ease the bones lightly with the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and dressings as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galien says, which is drier; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put below the head of this lens-shaped incisor, because this is its form. 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut at one part, and is the part sharp in II costs, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below; if it is adherent to the bone, then gently remove it, because one removes it well without pain, and without fear.  
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce to the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to apply that rasping, and remove the flakes with a fine scraper which you must have various quantities, to administer in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If one shaves before with coarse razors, and after with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, it is fitting that you bring cause according to its arrangement; and this thing is not replied to him who has put his study in this art.  
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, it behooves you to take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in II or III, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so that you do not hurt the wound, then administer by means a bandage from above, and do not tighten it further than is necessary to hold the wound alone; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of verbena, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer more medicinal ointments without mordication; and see that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor allow any pus to accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain's cloth, it breaks through and poisons, causing great harm to the patient; for when one puts something biting on the wound, it stings from above.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take therefore, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, then it is doubtful without a doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus does not come forth except because of the medicine that one has put on, which it has virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil, and glue I drapel, and put it on the sore; then cure it in the ways of cures as is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the bone above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.  
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it behooves you to thrust your little finger or needle into the two pieces, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and on the thumb outward, until the two rejoin according to their natural form; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain by your work.  
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and it cannot come to its place, then you must set it equal at the head of a stick somewhat thick. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another splint, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed, then bandage with two tents of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one over another, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the veins.  
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the making of auburn of an egg, and of powdered mill; then leave the tent, until the bone is hard, and the cartilages hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in goose feathers instead of tents, and if one winds the cloth around it, and holds the burn together, and breathes on the patient’s side; do as you see fit. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil comes while you are working on it, put some cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in the place of diaquillon. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put light poultices on top, and do not bind it at all; and if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for this, then sew up the fissure, and cure it with appropriate things such as bandages and ointments; and if it has no wounds inside, cover it with tents, and put piles of sponge inside, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated down, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outwardly so, and not broken in two, except that it buckles inward, if one knows lightly of it. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture gently inward, and hold it with the other hand from outside, and make it even. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension of the two parts, until they are equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, then strain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw cerote, and put on the double drape; and put on the drape a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what is changed; and put a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerote; and put on top a light linen bandage, and if the plasters stick, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward oneself none of the bone in it is taken away; so subtle of the take with instruments convenient to that. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, so sew up the wound if it is wide, and place upon it plasters suitable to those, in order to prevent suppuration, until it be healed.  
de la forcele	of the forceps 
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to III manners: or it is broken and separated into II, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is so when the fracture is without wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the fractured force; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then put equal the fracture to your hands, so that the form be as it is right, and there is no appearance nor deviation. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be it large according to your necessity; and being and light the force, and restrain the sphere in your hand, so that you put equal the fracture, as it is fitting. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus with force because it comes in contact, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his arm and put under the shoulder the pillow medium, and throw the ministers the shoulder down, until the bone of the humerus be lifted. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the fracture to your two hands, and if you find it shattered, it is necessary that you split it further; and gently treat the pieces, and if the bones cannot join due to any elevation, then cut one of the incisions that you have made; but that you put under the force of this instrument, in order to support the joint.  
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And seems like a spoon, and is not yet finished, and be also as wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so sew the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes to it, then soak the cloth in rose oil and wine, and put it on top.  
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of egg white, and put light dressings on top, and put a spear under the ass, if you need it; then take a very wide bandage of a palm width, then put I double drape over the dressings, and the plaster; then take a strip subtle of III fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging; and put the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the neck, and under the healthy ass, and under the diseased ass; and bind it from each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then rewind it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small cushion under the ass, to raise the shoulder upward; so it will lighten the fracture of the force by the relief of the shoulder, or you bind his arm to his neck, and do not unbind it until a bad accident comes, up to XX days; then start again the plaster, if you see that he needs it, and restrain it and leave it so, until it is restored; and she is restored at most in XXVIII days, and less for some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes it happens that the shoulder breaks or displaces in the middle, and it is known only by touch; if you prepare it according to the figure of the fracture, and set it back according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put above a double cloth. Then put upon a wide and fine board, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the board touches anywhere on the shoulder, so use hair from those places for padding, so that the board sits evenly; and then bind it firmly with a very strong bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and watch the joint every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and put back the board if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or in 25. And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, because it is not bone that sets itself easily astray.  
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, do it as above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the thigh to appease an abscess hot. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot 
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks down to the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of alacrity, and thirst, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the seams in the broken bone, and he feels all bad. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies flat on his back, and one puts a cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and subtly tries to put everything in all ways as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages above the delicate skin of salt, or another light, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the sling around the back, and hold it tight, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it softens, hold it tighter; and if it becomes necessary to untie it, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, and clean what has come there in ways of cures; then reapply the plaster, and hold it tight until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only to their thick parts after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only because they are glassy; and one feels it well upon inquiry as the two sides. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly as it should be. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint, and restrain it with a strap, if you need it.  
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declining inwards, the patient feels great pain and stinging, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and also pains, and coughs and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, in order to expel the wind outward.  
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not perform this, except abscesses are present if they have not arrived. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to him, heal it.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that some put cupping glasses on the area, to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw out superfluities from the place for the disposition of weakness.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of us should cover the place with soft wool in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make the wound even, then it is cured by the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain which he cannot suffer from the bone which points to the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut on the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under it an instrument to guard the flank; and then one must trench the bone, and extract lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with plasters, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put it on soft cloths in rose oil, and put it on the place; and cure while the place of this that it is appropriate to the abscess, and be lying still on the side where it must, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a break occurs in the bone of the neck, and sometimes it bends; and also in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if he will be healed or not, if you take notice if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many positions, and if they move and feel well when they are restrained and pulled, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if one puts care to it. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is sound or not, if you take care if its parts are soft, and if the accident which is in hands, and on its back there are gusts of wind and ejection without volition; and when one supports it on its belly, there is ejection without volition. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and he wants to sit, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if he does not labor in its cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then it is the lighter thing. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine oil rose or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound on the heart; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure it with ointment preventing flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your fist of your left hand in, and set it equal to the other hand at your power, then place the splint and bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do the same again, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, it does not happen except for a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the side, and comes to the patient pain at the place, and tingling, and inflates what breaks. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are over the fracture; and know what is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the top, put equal the fracture, as long as it is to natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it bends inwards, then make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, place it on the plaster, then place a splint of wood or of keel, and hold the splint so that it does not move; and employ the position under the ribs, as long as the limb is even. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
