Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come to it, do not touch them until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain as is fitting, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder  
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of two ways: one of which is that you take a piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with two bindings, and raise them up, and place the patient on a bench; then put one arm of the broken arm on the staff, as far as it comes to the armpit, and has half a curve of staff, then put on any heavy thing or the ministers extend it downward; then put the fracture together with his hands equally, until the fracture returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his bed, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands his ministers that one holds that which is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below to all the limb, and extends each one to his part. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, restrain the linen below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the shoulder head, it is necessary that you put one linen medium under the seat and the other towards the side, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the side, it is necessary to put the linen lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on top and on the side; then set the fracture as it should, and restrain it, unless an abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes there, do not restrain it until VII days, and put on a soft linen cloth in oil and rose water, until the abscess is appeased; then you shall restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you put the splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape on, and restrain it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm be in its place as long as nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves not, so use splints, and put upon the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint I finger's breadth of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the fracture III fingers on each side; then strain upon the splints, even as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, more strongly and less in moving.  
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess hot, then let it be tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the binding, that itching nor swelling come not at the place, or that the pains ne may come to the limb for those k’it is too strained. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the direction, as we have said.  
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, then do not untie it before three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; if it is addressed by virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have mentioned before, in such a manner that the meat be at first thin; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days after all; and therefore one must unbind and administer baths and medicines of ointments to bring the place together. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and entangled, it remains to untie for one or two months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of II bones, which are called the two «fosciles», because one is small, and it is the one that follows the pouch; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little joint; by chance breaks the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more grieved than when they are broken together.  
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended, and set straight. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great socket, then it is necessary to pull more strongly; and extend it on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers' arms to the part below his hand, or to the loin, and one other minister to the other above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if any are severed that grip the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make it up with bone as we have said before.  
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it comes with a fracture to a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then glue a pad made from rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the pad above subtly, until the abscesses are calmed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then put on the cerote and put the mold powder with abundance of egg yolk, then put the splints, and let the splint be on the top more outside, and one piece wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in more shapes: whether the fracture is in one bone, or two; and tighten more above the fracture than elsewhere, and all days less away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloth that are on the splint be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is strained, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you rise the limb of hot water, until that itch be appeased; and leave the member not a little rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loose and the bones out of place, and similar things, so address it.  
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And take care if the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too far away, then you must soften it a little, and leave it so for some days, until the nourishment comes back, and then restrain it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not unbind him until XX days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when it is a sprain then he should put his hands on his neck and be his neck even and beware of movement and shaking and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.  
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on our wrists many fractures occur, and there comes nothing but swelling many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit crossed, and be straight in front of him also; then put his hand on the board stretched out, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and place them equal to the joints, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and the bandages, if abscesses do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the length; and be wrapped in linen cloth.  
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the place between the belly and the root of the foot, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to tighten it to his broken part; then strain with a long cloth, and let the pad be as large as the palm of the hand, and restrain it, as it is fitting. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie tightly around the hand, and make the bandage tight between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our two hands, if it is the pouch, set it straight, as it is right; and hold it with the plant, and if you see that it puts a small straight piece to raise the fracture, and does not move; and if the fracture is to the other two, such as in the index or one of the others, set it straight, and tie it with the healthy hand that is after; or you tie them all in holding, which makes worth, or put on a splint, like the pouch; and take care in the restoration and disposition of hot and dry abscess, and support what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it can be seen well when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is made one part above the fracture, and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his leg to his side equally; and this is when the fracture is set in the bone.  
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, so one of the ligaments toward the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then be the ligaments next to the knee, and be the extension down; then put the mirrors the bone equal with his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the tie, if an abscess does not come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your cure; the stitch is made in such manner.  
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap on the fracture I bandage hard doubled in II or III, and in keep the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put I long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the thread upwards; then turn up the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the place eight between the leg and the hip of cloths soft to put equal tightness, then begin to tie firmly III turns or IIII on the fracture; and as much as you go higher above the fracture, and less tightness; then take hold of the II ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and in tie III splints that are above, then return down to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it so, until there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor other semblance. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then untie it, and place it where it comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then it is fitting to sew them together, if one can; and if one cannot, then it is fitting to split the place, and drain pus; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken in this way, as in the shoulder and arm; however, when restored in this manner, it does not ring the patient.   
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And knows that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the path of the knee 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times.  
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer just a fissure, or perforation, and it happens to every wound, and without wound, and this one feels well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal what is rounded to its parts, as much as it can be assembled moved; then put the splint, and on it put a round felt, if you have need of it, and restrain it as it is proper, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other breaks, such as hot poultice and similar; if put to each accident what he needs, until it is healed.  
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called by right “mustelz”, and the other is called “foscile”; and it has all alike fracture as it comes to the arm, and for that reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the works are all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, it turns the leg in every way.   
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, it turns forward. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is seen well; and it turns downwards.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer extension, and set it even, and bind the bones evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the bandage according to your virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two bandages of flexible wood that support the leg on one side and the other, and be long from the knee down below; then wrap them around with two bandages above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not be able to decline either to the right or to the left, and so it is well; and none administer a stick along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and put it on the leg to ward off movement, and properly done in the fracture or where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so cure until it is healthy.  
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones of the foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but to the bones of the foot come at any time fractures and to two points, and there have been further than in more postures. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there happens to the bones of the foot a fracture, and you see these bones overlap each other, put so the patient's foot on the earth, as if he wanted to go, and then put now your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their places; then put the splint and poultices on top, and under the belly of the foot a small board at II chiés plains, then restrain the foot carefully, then that you have wrapped bandages around, and other things which you have need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when III days or IIII will have passed, then untie the linen, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the legs broken, restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken leg a splint according to the length of the leg, and be one finger wider, then put under the foot the board that I have said, and strain evenly; and if there are II or III, or more, broken, put on each leg a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and strain the board under the foot; and let it stand on the head of the board away from the belly of the foot, so that it holds well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to the other fractures, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident as it is necessary. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the break of the bone of the finger 
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, so make her sit enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and be held behind; then fill the vagina of the woman with cotton, and put in it as large as a stick; then turn the woman over, and lift her back up and down, and then push the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the stick; and when she wants to pee, remove the cotton, and when she has peed, put it back, and so do for VII days or around: so will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of lamb, and tie to the hole a chain, and put the whole bladder in the nature; then blow into the chain form, until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these fractures near are not concealed from him who puts his study and use to them, and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For because the fracture signifies more than one way of restoration let us therefore 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the leg, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the leg; then wrap bandages around it, and let it stay for three days or until it is covered, and it will be healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the wounds that we have said testify to them. 
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, keep the vitriol there, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the broken bone that same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come there, let the restoration remain until the ninth day, so long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it neither on the third nor on the fourth day, for you would make it come bad accident. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then it behooves you to set it gently with your hands, with slight extension.  
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not prepared for you to put even with your hands, then remove it with this instrument which is of iron, which has VII or VIII of length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that the mirror takes III or IV, according to what he needs in each cure of bruise; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and be acute at the front, and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," for which the shoulder blade should be placed on top of the visible bone; and pull it at once, until it returns, and it is equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it behooves you to chop the head of the bone, until the instruments have purchase. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incision or a saw, to your power; then remove what remains in the bone of asperities and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.  
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so until it is in its place, then wet I drape the limb with black spiced wine, and properly that is how it should be; and do not put on the wound anything like cerote or anything else where there is oil, so that it does not cause decay and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and tell well the patient that the wound should not be strained with the fracture; and many times those who did this foolishly, and put on the patient either death or corruption at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more gentle than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put on stitches; but surround, instead of stitches, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, remove what you have placed on top of all the wine, and put ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmasion and similar.  
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and healed. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bone comes down gently.  
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days it passes and it cannot be mended back in place, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must close the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.  
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and other similar bones of the great limbs, do not treat it, for many times death comes from it. But leave it until it mends; perhaps it will mend by itself after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, let it be.  
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from the suture 
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the figure of the limb; and by chance cannot make the members its natural works. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward then if it is fresh: if administer medicinal astringents such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, in that way you take any of these things, or all together, and you confit them with astringent wine or with an abundance of egg or with basil; and put them on the knot in poultices, and hold it well, and do not untie it in your hands for days; and then undo it, and begin another, as long as the swelling is gone; or you restrain yourself to a piece of well-made wood; for the properties of the wood are that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then scoop above it, and make the superfluity apparent; or you put it on any razor, as long as it is gone, and the cure as long as it is healed.  
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and after that the limb remains weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not tied as it should; or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment cannot come to the limb; or because of too much inflammation; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood multiplies in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and ease; then put wool on the limb, so that the wool attracts to the great swelling, and the rose often of boiling water, until the swelling corrects to the limb; and returns to its natural figure. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After health, the crooked limb 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, however it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and brings great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the nodules and the torture are fresh, then it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of wormwood, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and you make the mollifying plaster, such as diaquilon well made, and you take the mash of wormwood, and you confit it with gelatine fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster above; or you take fig fats, and grind them with colon straw, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.  
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and lengthwise with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is entrenched and hardened, just like a stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it should be covered until the bone, with a subtle and light incision tool; and put care and study into the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is an issue from any joint of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is badly formed, and the patient feels great pain and great injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it is necessary now to bring back without tarrying. 
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, then the limbs swell, and by chance if it is reset it brings pain to the place; for this reason, it does not behoove us to move it when it is swollen: many times it causes inflammation and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave him, until the abscesses are calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as it comes in its place.  
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens sometimes that the jaws are dislocated, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: or they are a little displaced from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down toward the lower jaw, and cut off the saliva of the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and surrounds its tongue with the word. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many disarrangements. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it carefully and do not hesitate; and in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and puts his fist into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands be outside, to put equal; and command the patient to soften its mandibles, and moves them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the member is placed evenly, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back broken, even if it is the two jaws together, then bring hot water and oil to it, as long as you gently reset it; do not regret bringing it back, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with softening, he puts on soft cloths in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then binds it lightly with soft bindings; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his jaws be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he try to open his mouth, but eats light food, as long as the pains are gone, and the mandibles are healed; and then chew what he wants lightly, and do not work to open the mouth for eating and drinking, as long as the mandible is well healed and cured. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set back in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and familiar fevers come, and perhaps a bowel rupture, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times die those who have it, in nine days.  
de la forcelle	of the fork 
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The wrench cannot dislocate from within the ribcage, continuing into the flank, and it is dislocated no times outwardly, and one feels this well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies softly on his back, and stretches out his arms; and then presses the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it; and the shoulder which is towards the side cannot dislocate; if however, it dislocates any time, reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way is brought back the shoulder, when it is dislocated from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it is dislocated to the part of the seat towards down; and the second is to the part of the hip; and by adventure dislocated to the upper part, and this happens little; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, nor forward for the nerves; and many times dislocated downwards towards the seat, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it goes easily; in those who have enough flesh, it goes with difficulty, and returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men a percussion or fracture, and inflates the shoulder with a hot abscess, and believes that it is dislocated because of this.  
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it behoves you to examine it carefully, until you are certain; and then commence treatment.  
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocation when it is down towards the seat, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the seat to touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were one bone; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to its place, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly touching; and this manner of dislocation is not amiss to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is sick.  
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient up, then puts the fists under the seat, and lifts the joint with force upwards into its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and stretches it upwards, then puts it down; so come gently. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and administer a softening and soothing ointment, such as decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and administer it; then lie down the patient on his back, and put under his buttocks a pad of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of his heel on the pad, and raise the head of the shoulder carefully, and draw the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that he does not move backward; the shoulder returns now, and if you see it is not moving in this way: and that you do make a man present who is larger than the patient; and be straight towards the ribs, and put his shoulder under the buttocks of the patient, and raise the buttocks up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister draws the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may put with him any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another manner: and one takes a long stick in the ground, whose head is as if the handle of a pistol, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the sick person, but that he has cloths above, and the sick person lies on the long side of the stick; then his hand is stretched out on the other side, forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to come back for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a stick from the two arms of great size and four fingers wide, which has the rounded head to enter in the middle under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then on the head of the staff drapes a cloth so that the staff does not bleed the patient, then place it below the seat of the patient; and extend his arm upon the staff of length, and tie the assistant upon the staff, and the arm to the end of the hand, then put the arm upon the step of an ass's stirrup, and let be extended the hands down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint returns now. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that it is, it behooves you to put under the shoulder cap a ball of wool even, then put the plaster sprinkled with powder of the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the shoulder evenly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he massage little, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal faster; and then massage more after V days or VII, and move it; and if it is stiffened and is not softened, then it is healed.  
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is displaced from its place due to moisture that has come or for another cause, then you must administer cautery to it in three places, as it is shown in the chapter of cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and it unbinds after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint is never fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the hip, and the arms, or behind, is done by pushing and stretching of hands, and it is administered in another place; and care is taken until it is healed.  
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the limb, and gradually in movement, so the patient uses baths many times, until that pain is soothed, and returns to its first nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the cost  
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the knee is dislocated in some places, and in some places it returns; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, even at the front and back, and the dislocation is not put back in place, because one sees it well and feels it well; and dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the blade with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.  
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as abscesses come to it, because if abscesses came to it, it would be grievous to bring it back; and by adventure it cannot be brought back entirely at all, especially when it is in the rear; so it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by adventure it comes to death. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and its arms be spread, and the hands do mire according to the cut around, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and grasps the root of the palm with his knife that is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold them, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in each direction, then while you have enveloped a double long and wide sheet; and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, he puts oil of any kind to soften the joint, then put the joint back together, until it returns; and when it is in its place, he puts dry plaster on top with egg white, and strains it tightly, and bends the arm at the neck of the patient, and lets him for some days, then unties. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the ligament, and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well tightened, begin again with the splint and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, bathe him well and rub him, and press until he is soothed; or you put on the joint a fleece of fat sheep, then let it for a day and a night, then take it off, and he lets it enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the fleece back on, and then enter the bath; and thus do II times or III, until he is healed; and if you see, put on a wad of wet hot flax with butter, and strain it on; so it will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocated, and the return is light, more than the other joints Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the place becomes inflamed or that an abscess comes to it hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he puts it straight, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it as far as it returns; it is necessary that you look whether it is well in place; then put the sick person's back of his hand on a table at extension and reduction. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, the patient puts the back of his hand on the table, and the helper puts his hand on the appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. If not, then apply soothing plasters to the abscess and let him be until he begins again.  
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then the joint remains twisted; and does not harm the patient except that as long as the hand is weak, and cannot grasp anything at all: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other means except to restrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps there is no other thing. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then hold it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and let it be as such.  
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, apply the hot water cloth, and rub it until it is healed.  
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	At no time are the joints of the hand dislocated on either side, at no time on the back of the palm or on the belly; therefore they are the joint, and drive the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the joint, and the bend toward the part where it is disjointed; and leave it II days, and then put it equal that day; and do not tie it, as we have said, and untie it every day, and make it move, and tie it again; and do this often, until it is tight, and just as well do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and just as well do, when it is dislocated elsewhere. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the limbs jump and move without will, and cannot be held, and many times are softened any member, or the two hips or the two arms or one 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said there are many ways of treatment with great words, in which there is no profit at all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the inflammation that comes to the chest before, there is nothing that heals; and also that which comes straight to the II ribs, and one can only cure properly that which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be extended on his face in I place equal, and have restraint below him, so that he does not move; then put I stick at the head in earth forming, and the other as foot, and tie a bandage between the shoulders of the sick man, and the other to the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers tighten the bandages, one at the head and the other as foot, among the II sticks; and be well closed, the stick as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine forming, until it regains.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of three arms long, and place it under the armpit, and have the patient be on his side, and put the head of the board under the armpit, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and put the feet of the patient on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do it with the turn-key which turns by hand.  
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you put II sticks at the chief of the patient's arm of great, and towards the feet II others, and have between each stick, above and below, a palm's width of long; and have in each stick I hole, where the rope goes through, and let the sticks be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each II sticks have I turning stick, for which the ropes turn, and have in II turning II small sticks of a palm of long, to turn the rope; and then tie the rope that is among the ankles to the rope towards the chief, and the other rope towards the feet to the other rope, and each of the ministers turns his rope to all the rope, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said.  
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
