And when it is even, he places a desiccant plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the bandage of a tablet of III inches long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine straight, then tie it with a linen, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if any thing comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes comes the appearance in the back spine of the back, and they think that it is dislocations; and this is the bone which opens, so one should not have presumption: by chance would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only as dislocations, nor do they come out like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inward and outward, and front and rear; and more inward then, and less dislocated front and rear. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joints the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee; and it is swollen which is below inflamed by abscesses because the head of the hip comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to the fever, so is this accident contrary to these before. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has this in front, it is that his leg is well according to the accomplishment; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants him to go forward, he cannot before, and he holds back his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it in back, is that he cannot extend his knee nor double, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the hip joint is in place below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The returning of this sort of dislocation is that you observe if the dislocation is old and it remains according to its position, then there is no treatment needed; and it does not need for it to have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are IIII ways of dislocation, so hasten that you return the joint, and the extension within and without, and the movement to right and left; by chance it may return, and has no need of other cure. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you appear as the strong minister, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or to the linen that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he throws his hands below his shoulders, then he tightens with a firm linen strip above the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend up and down at once, until the patient is raised from the earth at once, and remain hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not done, it is necessary to take care of its appearance. When the dislocation is at the bottom, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen on the root of the hip, and the place that is below the angle, then extend the linen upwards towards the angle, and towards the forcele; then take other ministers with his arms, and embrace the thick place of the damaged hip, and extend it outwards: now it will return to its place; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, then it befits you to tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen cloth above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two more spans than the other; then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers hang with the patient, who together embrace the hip, for now the jointure returns readily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at its worst, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has glibosity, and strain the leg above the injured leg properly, and on the foot too; then put two sticks, one at the head and the other at the feet, then stick one stick between the thighs of the patient amidst the form; and make a bandage of moist cloths around, so that he does not freeze the injured person, then extend each minister towards him, and the mire puts equal to his hand the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it is not, place on, that is, a table, and press as we have said in the chapter of the boil, and the patient lies on their healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the mirror on his pain to be above the sick angle, then press with the other hand, and the estent down towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it does not become necessary to extend the patient down or lift up on the ground, but it becomes necessary that he be as if the hip were dislocated in the back, as we have said about bedding on the two hips; and let it be on its face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint to the table; and it will be at a point when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal; then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strain of a band, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then untie it, and put the splint on top; and if you see that they are equal, tie it up as before, and let him leave it for three days; then untie it, and let them go well, until the limb is strengthened.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.  
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if he does not hold at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as far as he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your two hands, then bend the two bones forming the knee; and one other minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he holds his leg at his hip lightly; and put the plaster on it, and make the leg adhere to the hip, and let them bind together strongly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not have the patient work hard to walk, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel 
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside. 
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it presses forward to the part where it is dislocated: the reattachment is light, and one must extend it gently with their hands when it is only moved slightly. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, it is necessary that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with the left twice, then upwards, and push the foot well upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, because it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put the post firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie wraps around it, so that the patient does not move; then hold the thighs by the ministers, and some other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the thigh, so that they bind it above the ankle of the foot; then extend all the ministers equally, and the posts be well between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when we are extending; then put the ministers the dislocation in their hands, and some other ministers hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return easily. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is well pointed, put the plaster and bandages on top, and hold it firmly, and tie his foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the ankle behind, that the ligature be not too tight; then leave it II days or III, and if the ligature softens, tighten it again; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for IIII days; and if he goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come there, then it is fitting that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed. 
des dois	of the two 
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and this is a light thing.  
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table straight, and put your foot on what opens those joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is aligned, and there is nothing open, then place under the sole of the foot a board at the shoulder, then restrain it firmly, and let it stay for 3 days, then untie it; and let him rest, as long as he is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not kind and merciful and tardy, nor rash; and use at the beginning soothing things a hot abscess, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then set the limb back in place, so that the abscesses chapped come; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things a hot abscess, and cure the wound as it is fitting, with dried ointments; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, put them together, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it will cost you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and of your body.
